Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi: Lineage and Nisbas
Biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi with his lineage and nisbas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly credentials of Imam al-Sanusi as reflected in his epithets and nisbas, and how his lineage connects him to both Berber tribes and prophetic descent.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi’s names and titles reveal his mastery of multiple Islamic sciences.

Before studying Imam al-Sanusi’s theological works, it is essential to know the man behind them. This introductory passage presents his full name, his many scholarly titles, and the meaning of his nisbas (attributive names). Understanding these nisbas helps us appreciate his place in the Maliki and Ash‘ari traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Notice the sequence of epithets and nisbas.
Pay attention to the structure: first the epithets, then the name, then explanations of nisbas.
2
Identify the epithets and their significance
The passage begins with a string of titles. List them and think about what each tells us about al-Sanusi’s expertise (e.g., 'shaykh mutakallimi' indicates his leadership in kalam).
3
Understand the nisba 'al-Sanusi'
The passage explains that 'al-Sanusi' comes from a Berber tribe. Note the different opinions on whether he was from them or just lived among them.
The footnote about his mother being a Sharifa connects him to the Prophet’s family.
4
Understand the nisba 'al-Tawhidi'
The passage explicitly says 'al-Tawhidi' refers to occupation with the science of tawhid. This is a key indicator of his specialization.
Avoid confusion with other uses of the term.
5
Reflect on the purpose of biography in kalam texts
Why do scholars include a tarjama? Consider how establishing the author’s credentials lends authority to the work.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في « تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية(١) ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية ((۲) ووجد بخطه على ( شرح الآجرومية » له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى(۳)
والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his age and his city, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the participator, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the fundamentalist, the verifier, the Sufi, the pious, the devout; Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. And 'al-Sanusi' is a relative attribution to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-Arus': 'To them is ascribed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them, and his mother was a Sharifa Hasaniyya (1), as verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Malali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (2). And it was found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isa al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I said: 'al-Isa is from the house of Isa (3).' And 'al-Tawhidi' is a relative attribution to occupation with the science of tawhid (theology), as mentioned by al-Hifnawi.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch (tarjama) of Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by listing his epithets: 'master of the theologians of his age and his city' (shaykh mutakallimi 'asrihi wa misrihi), indicating his preeminence in kalam (dialectical theology). He is described as an imam, all-knowing scholar (allama), participator (musharik, meaning he mastered multiple fields), hadith scholar (muhaddith), reciter (muqri'), jurist (faqih), fundamentalist (usuli, referring to legal theory), verifier (muhaqqiq), Sufi, pious (taqi), and devout (wari'). His full name is Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. The nisbas indicate his birthplace (Tilimsan/Tlemcen), his legal school (Maliki), his theological school (Ash'ari), and his specialization in theology (Tawhidi). The passage then explains the origins of the nisba 'al-Sanusi': it is derived from Sanusa, a Berber tribe in the Maghreb. He quotes al-Zabidi from 'Taj al-Arus' to clarify that al-Sanusi either settled among them or was from them. His mother was a Sharifa Hasaniyya (a descendant of the Prophet through Hasan). This is verified by al-Malali. Additionally, a note in al-Sanusi's own handwriting on his commentary of al-Ajurrumiyya gives his lineage as 'al-Sanusi al-Isa al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' The author comments that 'al-Isa' means from the house of Isa (presumably a family name). Finally, the nisba 'al-Tawhidi' is explained as indicating his engagement with the science of tawhid (Islamic theology), as mentioned by al-Hifnawi. This biography establishes al-Sanusi's authoritative credentials in kalam and related sciences.

Key Terms
سنوسي
مالكي
أشعري
توحيدي
ترجمة
متكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' refers to the philosophical school of Ibn Arabi.
Correction: The text explicitly states that 'al-Tawhidi' means occupation with the science of tawhid (Islamic theology), not adherence to Ibn Arabi's school.

Checkpoint
What does the nisba 'al-Tawhidi' indicate about Imam al-Sanusi?
A) He was a follower of the Sufi thinker Ibn Arabi.
B) He was specialized in the science of tawhid (kalam).
C) He was from the town of Tawhid in Morocco.
D) He wrote a book titled 'al-Tawhid'.

Key Takeaway
The nisbas of Imam al-Sanusi—especially al-Sanusi and al-Tawhidi—reveal his tribal origins and his specialization in the science of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi earned the nisba 'al-Tawhidi' by dedicating himself to the science of tawhid. If your life were summarized in a nisba today, what would it be—and are you content with that?
?
His mother was a Sharifa (descendant of the Prophet), yet he is recognized for his knowledge, not his lineage. Do you rely more on your background or on what you have actually studied and embodied of this deen?
?
The passage lists a chain of nisbas that define his identity. If you had to describe yourself by your relationship to Islamic knowledge, what would your 'nisba' be—and what is one step you will take this week to make that nisba more truthful?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Lineage and Nisbas of Imam Sanusi
Biographical introduction listing nisbas and their explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various nisbas (attributions) of Imam Sanusi and their meanings, including tribal, geographical, and scholarly attributions.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's name reveals his lineage, place, school, and specialization.

Imam Sanusi is known by multiple nisbas that each tell a part of his identity. This passage from his biography explains each attribution, citing authoritative sources like al-Zabidi's lexicon and notes from his own handwriting. Understanding these nisbas is key to appreciating his scholarly background.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the nisbas mentioned.
Pay attention to the full name and the attributions listed.
2
Identify each nisba
Go through each nisba: al-Sanusi, al-Tilimsani, al-Maliki, al-Ash'ari, al-Tawhidi, and the additional ones from his handwriting.
Notice how each nisba connects to a different aspect: tribe, city, school of law, theology, specialization.
3
Examine the sources cited
The biographer uses al-Zabidi's 'Taj al-'Arus' and al-Malali's 'al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya' to explain 'al-Sanusi'. Also, a note from Sanusi's own handwriting is referenced.
This shows the importance of citing authorities.
4
Reflect on the meaning of 'al-Tawhidi'
The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' is explained as indicating his expertise in the science of tawhid. Consider how this aligns with his reputation as a master theologian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي

شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدّث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي

والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في « تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية » ووجد بخطه على ( شرح الآجرومية ) له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى

والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي هذه النسبة له في « تعريف الخلف »

مولده ونشأته

ذلك اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي ؛ وسبب يرجع لعدم نصه هو على ذلك ، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً ،

قال العلامة التُنْبُكْتي في نيل الابتهاج : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة )

فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ٨٣٢هـ )

نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم ؛ فوالده هو الشيخ
Translation of Imam Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his time and his country, the imam, the all-knowing, the versatile, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the foundational legal scholar, the investigator, the Sufi, the pious, the devout: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. And 'al-Sanusi' is a nisba to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-Arus': 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them, and his mother was a noble Hasaniyya; thus it was verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Malali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya'. And it was found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. I said: 'al-Isi' is from the house of Isa. And 'al-Tawhidi' is a nisba to occupation with the science of Tawhid; thus al-Hafnawi mentioned this nisba for him in 'Ta'rif al-Khalaf'. His birth and upbringing: There is disagreement concerning the year of birth of Imam Sanusi; the reason for this goes back to the lack of his own statement on that, and the inconsistency of the transmission of his student al-Malali concerning that as well. The scholar al-Tunbukti said in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj': 'I saw a note from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Malali about the age of the Shaykh, and he said: He died at sixty-three years of age. So according to this narration, the year in which Imam Sanusi was born is 832 AH. Imam Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge; his father is the Shaykh
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Imam Sanusi. It begins by listing his honorific titles and his full name, including several nisbas (attributions): al-Sanusi (to the Berber tribe Sanusa), al-Tilimsani (from Tlemcen), al-Maliki (school of law), al-Ash'ari (theology), and al-Tawhidi (specialist in tawhid). The author then explains the nisba 'al-Sanusi' by citing al-Zabidi's lexicon, mentioning that Sanusi settled among the Sanusa tribe and may have been from them, and that his mother was a Hasanid sharifa. It also records a note from Sanusi's own handwriting on his commentary on the Ajurrumiyya, where he adds the nisbas 'al-Isi' (from the house of Isa) and 'al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' is explained as referring to his specialization in the science of tawhid, citing al-Hafnawi. The next section covers his birth: there is disagreement on his birth year because Sanusi himself did not record it and his student al-Malali gave inconsistent reports. The passage quotes al-Tunbukti, who reports that al-Malali said Sanusi died at age 63, implying a birth year of 832 AH. Finally, it notes that Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge, mentioning his father as a shaykh (though the text breaks off before naming him). The biography provides essential factual information about the scholar's identity and early life, relying on authoritative sources.

Key Terms
ترجمة
السنوسي
التوحيدي
تاج العروس
المواهب القدسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the nisba 'al-Sanusi' indicates a trade or city.
Correction: The passage explicitly states it is a tribal nisba to the Berber tribe Sanusa.

Checkpoint
According to the biography, what is the origin of the nisba 'al-Sanusi'?
A) A city in Morocco
B) A tribe of Berbers
C) A scholarly lineage
D) A Sufi order

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's full name and nisbas provide a detailed map of his lineage, tribal affiliation, school, and specialization.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam Sanusi is known by multiple nisbas that reflect his identity: his tribe, his school, his specialization. What labels or affiliations define your identity today? Are they based on lineage, knowledge, or something else? How can you ensure that your primary identity is rooted in your connection to Allah and His Messenger?
?
The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' shows that Imam Sanusi dedicated himself to the science of Tawhid. What area of Islamic knowledge are you most passionate about, and what is one concrete step you can take this week to deepen your understanding of it?
?
Imam Sanusi's mother was a Sharifa, connecting him to the Prophet's family. How does the legacy of the Prophet inspire you to improve your character and seek knowledge? What specific action will you take today to follow his example more closely?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Birth and Upbringing of Imam Sanusi
Biographical section on birth year disagreement and early upbringing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the uncertainty surrounding Imam Sanusi's birth year and the environment of knowledge in which he was raised.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's birth year is uncertain, but his upbringing in a family of learning is clear.

The biography next turns to Imam Sanusi's birth and early life. There is disagreement on his birth year due to lack of his own record and inconsistent reports from his student. The passage reports a narration that suggests he was born in 832 AH. It also emphasizes his upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on birth and upbringing
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the key points about his birth year and his upbringing.
Notice the two reasons for the disagreement.
2
Analyze the calculation of his birth year
The passage quotes al-Tunbukti that al-Malali said Sanusi died at 63, implying birth in 832 AH. Understand this inference.
This is based on a single narration, not definitive.
3
Reflect on his upbringing
The passage states he grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge, with his father being a shaykh. Consider how this environment shaped his scholarship.

Source Text

Translation of Imam Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his time and his country, the imam, the all-knowing, the versatile, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the foundational legal scholar, the investigator, the Sufi, the pious, the devout: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. And 'al-Sanusi' is a nisba to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. The scholar al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-Arus': 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them, and his mother was a noble Hasaniyya; thus it was verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Malali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya'. And it was found in his handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. I said: 'al-Isi' is from the house of Isa. And 'al-Tawhidi' is a nisba to occupation with the science of Tawhid; thus al-Hafnawi mentioned this nisba for him in 'Ta'rif al-Khalaf'. So according to this narration, the year in which Imam Sanusi was born is 832 AH. Imam Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge; his father is the Shaykh

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Imam Sanusi. It begins by listing his honorific titles and his full name, including several nisbas (attributions): al-Sanusi (to the Berber tribe Sanusa), al-Tilimsani (from Tlemcen), al-Maliki (school of law), al-Ash'ari (theology), and al-Tawhidi (specialist in tawhid). The biography provides essential factual information about the scholar's identity and early life, relying on authoritative sources.

Checkpoint
Why is there disagreement about Imam Sanusi's birth year?
A) He didn't record it
B) His student gave conflicting reports
C) Both A and B
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's birth year is uncertain, but his upbringing in a scholarly household shaped his future.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the uncertainty in Imam Sanusi's birth year, does it disturb your confidence in historical reports about scholars? How do you handle gaps in knowledge about your own spiritual lineage?
?
Imam Sanusi's upbringing in a household of virtue and knowledge shaped his future. Are you intentionally cultivating an environment of learning and piety for yourself or your family, or are you relying on chance?
?
The inconsistency in al-Malali's transmission reminds us of the fallibility of human memory. How carefully do you verify information about your religion before accepting it as truth? Will you commit to checking sources more rigorously?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
The Disagreement Over Imam Sanusi's Birth Year
Biographer presents conflicting reports on Imam Sanusi's birth year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why there is disagreement about Imam Sanusi's birth year and the two conflicting reports from his student al-Malali.

Core Idea
Even great scholars' birth years can be uncertain due to conflicting sources.

This lesson explores a biographical puzzle: Imam Sanusi's birth year is not definitively known. The passage presents two contradictory reports from his student al-Malali, showing how scholars handle such uncertainty. We will examine the reports and the cautious conclusion drawn by later historians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's presentation of the disagreement without immediately resolving it.
The passage is a historical note, not a doctrinal statement.
2
Identify the two reports from al-Malali
Find the two statements attributed to al-Malali about Imam Sanusi's age at death. What are the two ages mentioned?
One says 63 years, another says 55 years.
3
Understand the cause of disagreement
The author states the reason: Imam Sanusi did not specify his birth year, and al-Malali's transmissions are inconsistent.
4
Note the scholars' cautious stance
See how Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti resolved the matter by saying his birth was after 830 AH without pinpointing an exact year.
This shows scholarly caution in the face of conflicting evidence.
5
Reflect on historical methodology
This passage teaches that even for famous scholars, biographical details can be uncertain. Historians rely on weighing evidence and sometimes must settle for a range rather than a precise date.
The third report from al-Balawi (age 56) adds another possibility.

مولده ونشأته
ذلك اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي؛ وسبب يرجع لعدم نصه هو على ذلك، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً.
قال العلامة التُنْبُكْتي في نيل الابتهاج: (رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء: أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ، فقال له: مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة)
فعلى هذه الرواية: تكون السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام السنوسي هي ( ٨٣٢هـ )
وفي ( نيل الابتهاج ) ( ص ۵۷۰ ( أيضاً نقل قول الملالي: ( وأخبرني قبل موته بنحو عام أنَّ سنَّهُ خمس وخمسون سنة )، فتكون سنة ولادته على هذا ( ٨٤٠ هـ )، والله أعلم، ولهذا اكتفى ابن مريم والتنبكتي بقولهما: ( مولده بعد الثلاثين وثمان مئة )، وانظر ( البستان ) ( ص ٢٤٤ )، وعندما ذكر العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي خبر وفاته في ( ثبته ) ( ص ٤٣٨ ( قال: ( وكانت سنه يومئذ ستاً وخمسين سنة ) .
His birth and upbringing. That differed concerning the year of the birth of Imam Sanusi; the reason goes back to his not specifying it, and the inconsistency of the transmission of his student al-Malali concerning that as well. The scholar al-Tunbukti said in Nayl al-Ibtihaj: 'I saw a note from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Malali about the age of the Sheikh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years.' So according to this report, the year in which Imam Sanusi was born is 832 AH. And in Nayl al-Ibtihaj (p. 570) also a transmission of al-Malali's statement: 'He informed me about a year before his death that his age was fifty-five years,' so his birth year according to this is 840 AH, and God knows best. For this reason, Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti sufficed with their statement: 'His birth was after thirty and eight hundred.' And look at al-Bustan (p. 244). And when the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi mentioned the news of his death in his Thabat (p. 438) he said: 'His age on that day was fifty-six years.'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical discussion of Imam Sanusi's birth year. The author begins by stating that there is disagreement about the year of Imam Sanusi's birth, caused by the fact that the Imam himself did not specify it and by conflicting reports from his student al-Malali. He then quotes al-Tunbukti, who reports that al-Malali said the Imam died at age 63. Based on that report, the birth year would be 832 AH. However, another report from al-Malali, also in Nayl al-Ibtihaj, says the Imam was 55 at death, giving a birth year of 840 AH. The author notes that both reports are recorded, and some scholars settled by saying his birth was after 830 AH. He also cites al-Balawi's statement that the Imam was 56 at death. The passage thus presents the uncertainty without resolving it, showing scholarly caution.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the birth year of a famous scholar like Imam Sanusi is definitively known.
Correction: The passage shows that even for major figures, historical details can be uncertain. Imam Sanusi's birth year is not fixed; there are multiple conflicting reports.

Checkpoint

C) 832 AH and 845 AH
D) 840 AH and 850 AH

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi's birth year is not precisely known due to conflicting reports from his student; scholars cautiously place it after 830 AH.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam Sanusi's own student could not agree on his teacher's age. Think of someone you look up to in your religious life. Would you be able to accurately recount their life details? What does this tell you about your own fallibility in preserving and transmitting knowledge? Write down one step you can take today to be more precise when you speak about others.
?
When you hear a historical religious fact, do you accept it without question, or do you consider the possibility of human error? This passage reminds us that even great scholars like al-Malali made mistakes. How can you cultivate humility about what you think you know? Make a decision today to verify a piece of Islamic history you have assumed is true.

Imam Sanusi's Father and Early Teachers
Describes the piety and profession of Imam Sanusi's father and his early education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the family background and early educational environment of Imam Sanusi, including the piety of his father and his lineage.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's roots in piety and knowledge shaped his spiritual legacy.

This passage introduces us to the personal origins of Imam Sanusi. It highlights his father's character and profession, his family's spiritual lineage, and the environment of Tlemcen that nurtured his early education. By learning about his father's devotion and his teachers, we see the foundations of the Imam's own scholarly and spiritual path.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the biographical details sink in before analyzing.
Notice the description of the father as righteous, ascetic, and humble.
2
Identify key figures and places
Find who Yusuf Abu Ya'qub is, where Tlemcen is, and what the grandmother's lineage implies.
The title al-Husni comes from the Husayni lineage of his paternal grandmother.
3
Examine the quote from al-Malali
Read the quote describing the father's character. List the qualities mentioned.
This quote gives a vivid picture of his piety.
4
Understand the father's profession
Note that he was a Quran teacher for children. This shows his humble yet blessed occupation.
The passage mentions miracles and divine care associated with him.
5
Connect to the Imam's education
Reflect on how the Imam's early learning from his father and later from elite scholars laid the groundwork for his own scholarship.
The passage ends by mentioning his teachers and the attention of saints.

الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين.
وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنيَّة النسب، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه.
وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام: ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه .. رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً، خاشعاً الله تعالى، زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى، سالم الصدر، حسن الأخلاق، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه، حسن المعاشرة، كريم الطبع )
وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أن عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته.
شيوخه
أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلة علماء عصره، ونالته عناية ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين.
The righteous, the ascetic, the humble, the master, the investigator, Yusuf Abu Ya'qub. From him the Imam took the principles of the sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, and the clay of the saints and the righteous. And the grandmother of Imam Sanusi from his father's side was of Husayni lineage, thus the Imam Sanusi is sometimes called al-Husni from the side of his father's mother. And Sheikh al-Malali said in describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may God have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our Sheikh his son... was a righteous, devout man, humble before God, ascetic in the world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to God, sound of heart, good of character, smiling at everyone he met, good in companionship, generous in nature.' And the profession of this blessed father was teaching the Quran to children in the school. And it appears from the words of Sheikh al-Malali that the care of God accompanied him from his childhood, so God brought about miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight. His teachers. Imam Sanusi took knowledge from the elite of the scholars of his time, and he received the attention and glances of the saints and the righteous.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage provides a description of Imam Sanusi's family background and early education. First, it identifies his father as Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, a righteous and ascetic scholar from whom Imam Sanusi learned the basic sciences. The study took place in Tlemcen, a center of learning. Next, it mentions that his paternal grandmother was of Husayni lineage, which is why Imam Sanusi is sometimes called al-Husni. Then a lengthy description from al-Malali portrays the father as a model of piety, humility, and good character. His profession was teaching the Quran to children. The passage also notes that signs of divine care appeared in his life, including miracles and insight. Finally, it introduces his teachers, stating that he studied under the leading scholars of his age and was blessed with the attention of saints.

Correction: The passage clarifies that he was a simple Quran teacher for children, though he was highly pious and blessed.

Imam Sanusi's Lineage and Teachers
Biographical notes on Imam Sanusi's lineage, father, and teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of Imam Sanusi and the significance of his teachers in his formation as a scholar of Quranic recitation.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's authority in Quranic readings rests on a verified chain of teachers and a blessed upbringing.

This lesson introduces the personal and scholarly background of Imam Muhammad al-Sanusi. Before examining his theological works, it is important to appreciate the spiritual and academic environment that shaped him. The passage traces his family lineage, his father's piety, and his rigorous training in the seven Quranic readings under multiple masters.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical sketch
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the key events and names mentioned.
Notice the long chain of teachers and the emphasis on ijaza.
2
Identify the two key aspects
Notice how the passage covers both the Imam's family background (his father and grandmother) and his scholarly training (his teachers and ijazas).
3
Reflect on the chain of transmission
Consider the importance of the isnad (chain) in Islamic scholarship. How does this passage establish Sanusi's credentials?
The chain goes back through multiple masters.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب ، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم ، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها ، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين • وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنيَّة النسب ، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه ، وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام : ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه .. رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً ، خاشعاً الله تعالى ، زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها ، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى ، سالم الصدر ، حسن الأخلاق ، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه ، حسن المعاشرة ، كريم الطبع ) وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب ، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أن عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته ، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة « البقرة » ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما )
The righteous, ascetic, humble, verifying teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, from him the Imam took the principles of the sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge in its day, and the nature of the saints and righteous. And the grandmother of Imam Sanusi on his father's side was of Husni lineage, and thus the Imam Sanusi is sometimes called al-Husni from the side of his father's mother. And Shaykh al-Mallali said in describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our shaykh his son... was a righteous, pious man, humble before Allah, ascetic in [this] world, turning away from it, devoted to obedience to Allah, sound-hearted, good-mannered, smiling at everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature.' And the craft of this blessed father was teaching the Qur'an to children in the school. And it appears from the words of Shaykh al-Mallali that Allah's care accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah worked miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight. And Imam Sanusi had high standing in the compilation of the Qur'anic readings; for the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven readings from the jurist, teacher, scholar, practitioner, verifier, reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Husni, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: I added from a third a substantial amount whose limit I have not now verified, compiling the seven according to the contents of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he gave him a general absolute authorization in the seven readings and in other of his transmitted materials. And he narrated to him the seven from the two great imams and teachers: the venerable, most renowned, famous, verifying reciter, the penitent, humble Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasni, and the venerable, honored, famous, verifying, precise, proficient, grammatical, linguist, memorizer, righteous, pure Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn the jurist, scholar, versatile Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Laja'i. Recitation to the first as a compilation in one complete recitation of the seven, he said: I added three hizbs from Surat al-Baqara. And to the second for al-Fatiha, al-Baqara, and the beginnings of Al 'Imran, as a compilation of the seven, and authorization in what he recited and in what remained. Both of them narrated to him together that from the two teachers: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhut, with their chains.'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam Sanusi's scholarly lineage and teachers. It begins by identifying his father, Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, a righteous and ascetic teacher from whom the Imam learned the principles of the sciences in Tlemcen. It then notes that the Imam's paternal grandmother was of Husni lineage, hence his occasional title 'al-Husni'. Shaykh al-Mallali's description emphasizes the father's piety and good character. The father's occupation was teaching the Qur'an, and he was supported by divine care and miracles. The passage then highlights Imam Sanusi's expertise in the seven Qur'anic readings (Qira'at), quoting Abu Ja'far al-Balawi's account of his study under Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Husni, and his authorization (ijaza) from him. Al-Balawi also reports that Sanusi studied with two other masters, al-Yaznasni and al-Laja'i, detailing the specific portions recited. The chain of transmission is traced back to earlier teachers al-Qaysi and Ibn Mabhut. Thus, the passage establishes Sanusi's solid scholarly credentials in both spiritual formation and the science of Qur'anic recitation.

Correction: The text clearly states that his grandmother on his father's side was of Husni lineage, hence the title.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Imam al-Sanusi's Mastery of the Seven Quranic Readings
Biographical account of Sanusi's qira'at study

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the depth of Imam al-Sanusi's training in Quranic readings, including his teachers, the texts he used, and the nature of his ijaza.

Core Idea
Sanusi's qira'at training shows the rigorous chain-based transmission central to Islamic scholarship.

Imam al-Sanusi is known for his theological works, but this passage reveals his profound expertise in Quranic recitation. His study of the seven readings involved multiple teachers, complete recitations, and formal licenses. This section highlights the meticulous process of preserving the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of al-Balawi
Begin by reading the quote from Abu Ja'far al-Balawi. Note how Sanusi studied the seven readings under Abu al-Hajjaj al-Hasani, reciting the entire Quran twice.
Pay attention to the phrase ' جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية » '.
2
Identify the second chain
The passage then provides another chain through two teachers, al-Yaznasani and al-Lujai. Notice the details of what portions were recited to each.
This shows the multiple routes of transmission.
3
Understand the ijaza
Sanusi received a general absolute license (ijaza) from al-Hasani to teach the readings. Consider the significance of formal authorization in Islamic learning.
Ijaza connects the student to the Prophet through an unbroken chain.
4
Reflect on the texts used
The readings were combined according to al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. Think about the role of these classical works in standardizing qira'at.

وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية ) وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة « البقرة » ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي ، وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما )(۱) ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي والشيخ الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه « الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي « الإرشاد » لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد . واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه « الصحيحين » وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز له وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها . وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد
Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the collection of Quranic readings. The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven Quranic readings from the jurist, the teacher, the scholar, the worker, the verifier, the reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations of the Quran. He said: And I added from a third a significant amount whose limit I have not verified now, combining the seven readings according to the contents of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he [al-Sanusi] gave him a general absolute license in the seven readings and in other transmitted narrations. And he narrated the seven to him from the two eminent scholar-teachers: the lofty, most renowned, most famous reciter, verifier, insightful, humble teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasani, and the lofty, venerated, famous, verifier, precise, proficient, grammarian, linguist, memoriser, righteous, purest teacher Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Faqih al-'Alim al-Mutafannin Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Lujai, recitation to the first as a combined completion for the seven, he said: And I added three sections from Surat al-Baqara, and to the second for Surat al-Fatiha and al-Baqara and the beginning of Al 'Imran combining the seven, and a license for what he recited and what remained. Both narrated to him together from the two teachers: Abu Abdullah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhkhut through their chain of transmission.' Among the scholars from whom he read: the scholar Nasr al-Zawawi, the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, the sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani (he took from him the seven readings), the teacher Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn ibn 'Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab (he took from him jurisprudence), the equitable scholar Abu Abdullah al-Habbak (he took from him the science of the astrolabe), Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilimsani (he read to him principles, logic, rhetoric, and jurisprudence), the memoriser Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari his maternal brother (he read to him al-Risala, and he and this brother read to the pious righteous Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid). And he occupied himself with narration and sciences of hadith under the pious righteous teacher Abu Zaid Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alabi, and he narrated from him the two Sahihs and other hadith and tradition books, and he gave him a license for what he was permitted and from him, and he listened to the musalsalat and other things. And he read inheritance and arithmetic under the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he gave him a license for all that he narrated, and also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif gave him a license from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's extensive education. It begins by highlighting his high standing in the field of Quranic readings (qira'at). The author quotes the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who describes how al-Sanusi learned the seven canonical Quranic readings from the esteemed reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani. Al-Balawi notes that al-Sanusi recited the entire Quran to him twice, and added a significant amount from a third recitation, combining the seven readings according to the books al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. He also received a general absolute license (ijaza) to teach these readings and other narrations. Al-Sanusi further narrated the seven readings through al-Balawi from two other eminent teachers: Abu al-Abbas al-Yaznasani and Abu al-Abbas al-Lujai, with details of what portions were recited to each. The passage then lists other scholars from whom al-Sanusi read various sciences: he studied qira'at again with Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani (the same teacher mentioned earlier), jurisprudence with Abu Abdullah al-Maghili (al-Jallab), astronomy with Abu Abdullah al-Habbak, principles of jurisprudence (usul), logic, rhetoric, and fiqh with Imam Muhammad al-Tilimsani, and al-Risala (likely a Maliki text) with his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti. Together with his brother, he also read al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid under Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi. For hadith, he studied under Abu Zaid al-Tha'alabi, from whom he narrated the two Sahihs and other books, received a general ijaza, and listened to the musalsalat (chains of transmission). Finally, he studied inheritance law and arithmetic under Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who gave him a blanket ijaza, and he also received an ijaza from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif through his father. The passage demonstrates the breadth of al-Sanusi's education across transmitted and rational sciences.

Key Terms
القراءات السبع
الإجازة
التيسير
الشاطبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think learning qira'at is simply memorizing a single recitation, but the passage shows it involves multiple complete recitations and formal licenses.
Correction: Qira'at training required reciting the entire Quran multiple times to a master and receiving an ijaza, as Sanusi did with al-Hasani.

Checkpoint
How many complete recitations of the Quran did Imam al-Sanusi recite to Abu al-Hajjaj al-Hasani?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's mastery of the seven Quranic readings involved multiple teachers, full recitations, and authoritative texts, demonstrating the rigorous chain-based transmission of qira'at.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi tirelessly recited the Quran to multiple teachers to perfect his recitation. Reflect on your own recitation: have you sought out knowledgeable teachers to correct your pronunciation and tajweed? If not, what is holding you back from taking that step today?
?
The chain of transmission connects every reciter back to the Prophet ﷺ. Do you feel that you are part of that chain? If not, what is the first step you can take to attach yourself to it?
?
Combining the seven readings required immense discipline and dedication. Is there an area of your deen where you have been satisfied with mediocrity, rather than striving for mastery? What would change if you committed to excellence in that area?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

The Breadth of Imam al-Sanusi's Education Across Sciences
List of teachers and subjects in Sanusi's education

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the vast scope of Imam al-Sanusi's education, spanning jurisprudence, hadith, logic, astronomy, and more.

Core Idea
Sanusi's education was encyclopedic, integrating transmitted and rational sciences.

Having studied Quranic readings, Sanusi turned to a wide array of other disciplines. This passage lists numerous teachers and subjects, from Maliki fiqh to the astrolabe, showcasing the traditional Islamic curriculum's breadth.

Guided Path
1
List the subjects Sanusi studied
Scan the passage and identify all the subjects mentioned, from fiqh to arithmetic. Write them down.
Some subjects are explicitly stated, others implied by the teacher's expertise.
2
Identify the teachers for each subject
For each subject, note the teacher's name. Some teachers taught multiple subjects.
Pay attention to the chain for hadith and the final ijaza.
3
Note the types of sciences
Categorize the subjects into transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli) sciences.
This shows the balance in the traditional curriculum.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider what this variety tells us about Sanusi's intellectual training and the value placed on comprehensive education.
All these subjects inform his theological works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the vast number of teachers Imam al-Sanusi studied under, do you see your own learning as a solitary endeavor or as part of a chain? Are you actively seeking out living teachers and scholars to deepen your understanding, or relying solely on books and online resources? What one step can you take this week to find a guide in a specific Islamic science?
?
Imam al-Sanusi studied subjects ranging from Quranic readings to arithmetic. Look at your own knowledge: are you neglecting the 'rational' sciences (logic, language, etc.) that could strengthen your understanding of aqeeda? Is your study balanced, or do you focus only on what is easy or popular?
?
The passage mentions formal permissions (ijazat) given to al-Sanusi. When you learn something, do you seek to verify its source and chain? How can you ensure that what you believe and practice is based on authentic transmission, not just personal opinion or popular culture?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Imam al-Sanusi's Teachers and Sciences
Listing of Imam al-Sanusi's teachers and the sciences he studied with them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam al-Sanusi's traditional Islamic education through his teachers in various sciences.

Core Idea
A scholar’s knowledge is built on his teachers—Sanusi studied under masters of every major Islamic science.

This passage from Sanusi's biography lists the scholars he studied with, showing his comprehensive training in the Islamic sciences. Before diving into his theological works, it is useful to see the scholarly network that shaped him. The passage reveals his mastery of Qur'an, hadith, fiqh, usul, logic, rhetoric, astronomy, arithmetic, and more.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of the teachers and sciences. Note the footnote about Ibn Tumart to avoid confusion.
The start 'أحمد' may be a page header or part of a name.
2
Identify the main teachers and sciences
Go through the text and list each teacher and the science they taught. Notice the pattern 'أخذ عنه/عليها'.
Teachers include al-Zawawi, Ibn Tumart, Abu al-Hajjaj, al-Maghili, al-Habbak, al-Tilmisani, al-Taluti, al-Tha'alibi, al-Qalasadi, and Ibn Marzuq.
3
Understand the ijaza system
The passage mentions ijaza (permission) from al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi. Reflect on how this system transmitted knowledge from teacher to student.
Ijazas were a formal way of certifying that a student had mastered a text or subject.
4
Reflect on the breadth of Sanusi's education
Consider how studying with many scholars in different fields prepared him for writing theological works like his creedal treatises.
This diverse training is a hallmark of traditional Islamic scholarship.

قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من
أشياخنا وغيرهم ، ومن أكابرهم : ولي الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب ( نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) .
Ahmad (1) al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and the noble sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani – he learned from him the seven Qur'anic readings – and Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Maghili known as al-Jallab – he learned from him fiqh – and the upright scholar Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak – he learned from him the science of the astrolabe – and Imam Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilmisani – he read under him usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh – and the hadith master Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother – he read under him 'al-Risala', and he and his brother this one read under the pious imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kanabishi 'al-Irshad' of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of tawhid. And he occupied himself with hadith transmission and the sciences of tradition under the pious imam Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, and he narrated from him the 'Sahihayn' and other books of hadith and tradition, and he gave him permission for what he himself was permitted to transmit, and he made him hear the musalsalat and other things. And he read inheritance law and arithmetic under the eminent scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he gave him permission for all that he narrated, and likewise Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif gave him permission from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid (2). (1) It is said: 'Tuzat' instead of 'Tumart', and he is not Ibn Tumart the Mahdi of the Almohads, as is not hidden. (2) That was mentioned by the scholar Muhammad Makhluf in 'Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya' (1/387). 18. Al-Balawi said: 'He took from teachers of his town from a group of our teachers and others, and from their greatest: the friend of Allah, the pious imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas – and he did not take much from him and others – and he also took from our teacher Abu Abd Allah ibn Marzuq ibn Marzuq, and our teacher Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the jurist of furu' Abu Abd Allah al-Jallab, and the noble jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar' – I think he took from him – and he learned the science of arithmetic and inheritance from the jurist outstanding in them Abu Abd Allah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his brother previously mentioned, and from those whom his student, our companion, the noble, accomplished, blessed jurist Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in the book of introduction to him.'
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of Imam al-Sanusi's teachers in various Islamic sciences. It begins by naming several scholars from whom he studied: Ahmad al-Zawawi, Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji (with a footnote clarifying that this is not the famous Almohad Mahdi), the sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf (for Qur'anic readings), Abu Abd Allah al-Maghili al-Jallab (for fiqh), Abu Abd Allah al-Habbak (for astronomy), Muhammad ibn al-Abbas al-Tilmisani (for usul, logic, rhetoric, and fiqh), and his maternal brother Abu al-Hasan al-Taluti (for 'al-Risala' and 'al-Irshad' of al-Juwayni, as well as tawhid). The passage then describes his hadith studies under Abu Zayd al-Tha'alibi, from whom he narrated the Sahihayn and other works, and who gave him general permission (ijaza). He also studied inheritance law and arithmetic under Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, who also gave him ijaza. Another permission came from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif via his father. The second paragraph, quoting al-Balawi, adds additional teachers: Abu Ali al-Ahsan (Abarkan), Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas, Ibn Marzuq, al-Qalasadi, al-Jallab, al-Gharabili, and Ibn Tumart (for arithmetic and inheritance). It ends by noting that his student al-Mallali wrote a biography of him. This listing shows the breadth of Sanusi's education, covering Qur'an, hadith, fiqh, usul, logic, rhetoric, astronomy, and arithmetic, and his connection to many important scholars of the time.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji is the famous Almohad Mahdi Ibn Tumart.
Correction: The footnote explicitly says he is not the Mahdi; his name is sometimes written as 'Tuzat' and he is a different scholar.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi studied under a diverse group of scholars, mastering both transmitted and rational sciences, which equipped him for his later theological works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi studied under over a dozen teachers in a wide range of sciences. Are you intentionally diversifying your own Islamic knowledge, or are you content with only one subject? What step will you take this week to explore a field you have neglected?
?
This lesson shows that Sanusi not only learned from great scholars but also sought multiple permissions (ijazat). Do you take the time to properly honor and learn from each of your teachers, or do you rush through your studies without truly benefiting from their expertise? Write down one specific way you can improve your relationship with a current teacher.
?
Sanusi studied both transmitted and rational sciences, from Qur'an and hadith to logic and astronomy. Is your own pursuit of knowledge balanced between spiritual sciences and worldly sciences that serve your faith? What science are you avoiding because it seems difficult, and how can you begin learning it today?

Sanusi's Sufi Training and Key Influence
Discusses Sanusi's Sufi influences and highlights Ibrahim al-Tazi as his key spiritual teacher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sufi influences on Imam al-Sanusi, particularly the role of Ibrahim al-Tazi, and the practices he transmitted.

Core Idea
Sanusi's spiritual training was deeply rooted in a Sufi lineage centered on Ibrahim al-Tazi.

This passage reveals a lesser-known side of Imam al-Sanusi: his deep connection to Sufism. While he is famous for his kalam works, his spiritual formation was guided by saintly figures. The passage highlights Ibrahim al-Tazi as his most influential teacher and describes a small register of transmitted practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to grasp the overall meaning. Notice the names and practices mentioned.
This passage is biographical, not doctrinal, so focus on the historical details.
2
Identify the key spiritual influence
Look for the phrase that indicates who had the greatest impact on Sanusi in his Sufi upbringing. The passage explicitly names Ibrahim al-Tazi.
The passage says 'the one with the greatest impact' (صاحب الأثر الأكبر).
3
Examine the register's contents
Al-Kattani mentions a small register (thabt) that Sanusi compiled. Identify the hadiths and practices it contained: hadith of precedence, hospitality, handshaking, etc.
These practices are transmitted by way of al-Tazi.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this passage is important for understanding Sanusi's overall intellectual and spiritual profile. It shows he was not only a theologian but also a Sufi with a chain of transmission.
This corrects the common oversight of his Sufi side.

تصوفة وتربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنَّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي
نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من
هذا
الوجه
وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٢/ ٩٩٩ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
His Sufism and his moral upbringing. There are great spiritual figures by whom Imam al-Sanusi was influenced, but it appears that the saintly, gnostic, righteous elder Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanusi in this respect. And the scholar al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihris al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general permission from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi and Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi and others. He said: 'He had a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of precedence, the hadith of hospitality with the two black things, handshaking, interlocking fingers, wearing the patchwork cloak, giving the prayer beads, and instructing in dhikr by way of his teacher Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of Imam al-Sanusi's Sufi training and ethical formation. It begins by stating that while he was influenced by many great spiritual figures, the one who had the greatest impact was Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, a saintly scholar residing in Oran. The passage then quotes al-Kattani from his 'Fihris al-Faharis' to show that Sanusi had a small register (thabt) in which he recorded chains of transmission for specific hadiths and practices: the hadith of precedence (hadith al-awwaliyya), the hadith of hospitality with the two black things (dates and water), and practices such as handshaking, interlocking fingers, wearing the Sufi patchwork cloak (khirqa), giving the prayer beads, and instructing in dhikr. These chains went back to his teacher Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi. This illustrates Sanusi's connection to the Sufi tradition and his transmission of spiritual practices and hadiths with isnad.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi was solely a rational theologian with no Sufi dimension.
Correction: This passage shows he was deeply immersed in Sufi training, had a spiritual teacher (al-Tazi), and transmitted Sufi practices like wearing the khirqa and dhikr instruction.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual training was deeply rooted in the Sufi tradition, with Ibrahim al-Tazi as his key teacher and a register of transmitted practices linking him to the prophetic way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have a living connection to a teacher who guides your spiritual practices, or are you relying solely on books and your own efforts? What steps will you take this week to seek a living link to the prophetic way?
?
The khirqa, subha, and talqin al-dhikr are tangible practices transmitted through a chain. Which of your daily actions is consciously tied to a chain back to the Prophet ﷺ, and which are merely habitual? How can you bring more intentionality into your worship?
?
Sanusi's thabt shows he was meticulous in recording his spiritual lineage. If you had to write a 'register' of your own spiritual influences and practices, would it show a connected chain or a scattered collection? What is one gap you can address starting today?

Sanusi's Scholarly Teachers
Al-Balawi enumerates Sanusi's early teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key teachers from whom Imam al-Sanusi acquired his formal Islamic sciences during his early education.

Core Idea
Sanusi studied under a distinguished chain of teachers in various Islamic disciplines.

This lesson introduces the scholars who taught Imam al-Sanusi in his hometown, as recorded by al-Allama al-Balawi. These names reveal the breadth of his early training in fiqh, usul, arithmetic, and other sciences. The passage provides a glimpse into the scholarly network that shaped his intellectual foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Balawi uses a list format with brief details for each teacher.
2
Identify the teachers and their specialties
List each teacher mentioned and note any specific subject or contribution attributed to them in the passage. For example, Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart taught arithmetic.
3
Reflect on studying under multiple shuyukh
Consider why Sanusi studied with many teachers rather than one. What does this say about traditional Islamic education?
This connects to the learning objective about the breadth of his training.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم ، ومن أكابرهم : ولي الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب ( نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) . تصوفة وتربيته الأخلاقية هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنَّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٢/ ٩٩٩ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
Al-Allama al-Balawi said: (He took from the scholars of his country from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah the Exalted, the learned righteous imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him, and others. He also took from our shaykh Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq ibn Marzuq, and our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the jurist of furu' Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabli author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar' – I think he took from him – and he took the science of arithmetic and inheritance shares from the distinguished jurist in them Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his brother mentioned previously, and from these whom his student our companion the noble accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in the book of introduction to him.) His Sufism and moral training: There are great spiritual personalities whom Imam al-Sanusi was influenced by, but it appears that the saintly righteous knower Shaykh Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, had the greatest influence on Imam al-Sanusi from this. And al-Allama al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihris al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general license from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: (He has a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of priority, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, handshaking, interlocking, wearing the patched cloak, giving the prayer beads, and prompting the dhikr from the path of his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.)
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi's academic and spiritual education. It begins with a citation from al-Allama al-Balawi, who enumerates a list of shaykhs from whom Sanusi studied. The list includes both local scholars from his hometown and others from elsewhere. The first group includes figures like Abu Ali al-Ahsan (known as Abarkan) and Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, though it notes Sanusi did not take much from the latter. Further names are added from his teachers: Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the Maliki jurist Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabli (author of a versification of the Mukhtasar), and Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, who specialized in arithmetic and inheritance. The list also mentions Sanusi's brother and his student Muhammad al-Mallali, who compiled these names in a biographical work. The passage then shifts to Sanusi's spiritual training with the heading 'his Sufism and moral training', stating that many saintly figures influenced him, but the greatest impact came from Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi. A second quote from al-Allama al-Kattani provides additional teachers from whom Sanusi had a general ijaza (permission to transmit), including al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and notes that Sanusi had a small register containing chains for specific practices, which he received via al-Tazi. Together, these citations establish Sanusi's broad scholarly and spiritual lineage.

Spiritual Training and General Ijaza
Al-Kattani describes Sanusi's spiritual influences and his ijaza.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual mentors of Imam al-Sanusi and the concept of general ijaza as practiced in his tradition.

Core Idea
Sanusi's spiritual formation was profoundly shaped by Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi.

Beyond formal scholarship, Imam al-Sanusi underwent spiritual training under saintly figures. This lesson focuses on the greatest influence—Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi—and on the general ijaza (license to transmit) that Sanusi received from prominent scholars like al-Tha'alibi. It also highlights a small register of chains for specific practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on spiritual training
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice the shift from scholarly teachers to spiritual influences.
2
Identify the key spiritual figure
Find which teacher is described as having the greatest influence. Note his name and description.
The passage says Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi had the greatest impact.
3
Understand the general ijaza
Read about the general license Sanusi held from al-Tha'alibi and others. Also note the small register of specific chains.
General ijaza allowed him to transmit hadith and other knowledge from those scholars.

قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم ، ومن أكابرهم : ولي الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصالح أبو علي الأحسن المعروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب ( نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) . تصوفة وتربيته الأخلاقية هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنَّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران . . كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا وذكر العلامة الكتاني في ( فهرس الفهارس ) ( ٢/ ٩٩٩ ) أن الإمام السنوسي كان يروي بالإجازة العامة عن أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي وأبي الحسن القلصادي وعن غيرهما ، قال : ( وله ثبت صغير ذكر فيه إسناد حديث الأولية وحديث الضيافة على الأسودين والمصافحة والمشابكة ولبس الخرقة ومناولة السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
Al-Allama al-Balawi said: (He took from the scholars of his country from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their greatest: the saint of Allah the Exalted, the learned righteous imam Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him, and others. He also took from our shaykh Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq ibn Marzuq, and our shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the jurist of furu' Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabli author of 'Nazm al-Mukhtasar' – I think he took from him – and he took the science of arithmetic and inheritance shares from the distinguished jurist in them Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, and he also took from his brother mentioned previously, and from these whom his student our companion the noble accomplished blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali included in the book of introduction to him.) His Sufism and moral training: There are great spiritual personalities whom Imam al-Sanusi was influenced by, but it appears that the saintly righteous knower Shaykh Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, had the greatest influence on Imam al-Sanusi from this. And al-Allama al-Kattani mentioned in 'Fihris al-Faharis' (2/999) that Imam al-Sanusi used to narrate by general license from Abu Zayd Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alibi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and others. He said: (He has a small register in which he mentioned the chain of the hadith of priority, the hadith of hospitality on the two black things, handshaking, interlocking, wearing the patched cloak, giving the prayer beads, and prompting the dhikr from the path of his shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Tazi.)
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Sanusi's academic and spiritual education. It begins with a citation from al-Allama al-Balawi, who enumerates a list of shaykhs from whom Sanusi studied. The list includes both local scholars from his hometown and others from elsewhere. The first group includes figures like Abu Ali al-Ahsan (known as Abarkan) and Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, though it notes Sanusi did not take much from the latter. Further names are added from his teachers: Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq, Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, the Maliki jurist Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, Abu al-Faraj al-Ghurabli (author of a versification of the Mukhtasar), and Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart, who specialized in arithmetic and inheritance. The list also mentions Sanusi's brother and his student Muhammad al-Mallali, who compiled these names in a biographical work. The passage then shifts to Sanusi's spiritual training with the heading 'his Sufism and moral training', stating that many saintly figures influenced him, but the greatest impact came from Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi. A second quote from al-Allama al-Kattani provides additional teachers from whom Sanusi had a general ijaza (permission to transmit), including al-Tha'alibi and al-Qalasadi, and notes that Sanusi had a small register containing chains for specific practices, which he received via al-Tazi. Together, these citations establish Sanusi's broad scholarly and spiritual lineage.

أبو زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي
الإجازة العامة

?

The Virtues of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi and Sanusi's Companionship
A description of al-Tazi's virtues and Sanusi's association with him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the remarkable virtues of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi as described by his contemporaries and the significance of Imam al-Sanusi's companionship with him.

Core Idea
Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi was so renowned for his forbearance that his name became a proverb.

This passage from Sanusi's biography introduces us to a towering spiritual figure, Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi, whose virtues became legendary. Through a vivid quotation, we see how his patience, wisdom, and piety were so exemplary that people used his name as a benchmark for excellence. The passage also reveals that Imam al-Sanusi was among the blessed few who had the privilege of his companionship, linking Sanusi to a chain of spiritual masters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall sense, then read the English translation carefully.
The passage has a quotation within it; notice how it flows.
2
Focus on al-Tazi's virtues
Identify the specific virtues attributed to Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi, especially the proverb about his forbearance and intellect.
The proverb shows how he was regarded by the community.
3
Note the list of companions
The passage names several scholars who also had the honor of accompanying al-Tazi. Recognize that Sanusi is included among them.
This highlights the spiritual lineage and shared influence.

This aspect; for in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Qur'an and linguistics, and memorization of hadith, and the breadth of his knowledge in fiqh and its principles, and sharpness of his insight and understanding... he was endowed with the manners of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-Allama al-Tanbakti transmitted in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': (Sufficient for you regarding his majesty and happiness: that proverbs were coined about his intellect and forbearance, and mention of his virtue and knowledge spread in the horizons until now; if someone exaggerated in describing a man, he would say: 'He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi'; and if one of them became filled with rage, he would say: 'If I were in the station of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have endured this', because of what he bore of harm from people, patience in hardships, doing good to people, and forbearance. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller to spread his miracles, draped in the robe of love and awe, with the acceptance he has in the hearts of the elite and the common; so he called them to Allah with insight, and guided them to His worship through the doctrines of tawhid and the functions of dhikr.) And among the blessings of Imam al-Sanusi was his companionship with this noble knower and his affiliation with him, and he was joined in this by notable figures: like his maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a eulogy for Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi, detailing his virtues and his influence on Imam al-Sanusi. It begins by noting his excellence in Qur'anic sciences, linguistics, hadith memorization, fiqh and its principles, and his sharp intellect. Then it states that he was endowed with the manners of saints and perfected souls. A quotation from al-Tanbakti via Ibn Sa'd describes al-Tazi's legendary forbearance and wisdom: proverbs were coined about his intellect and patience, and people would compare others to him when praising forbearance. He is portrayed as a paragon of patience in the face of harm from others, performing good deeds, and maintaining gentle conduct. Allah manifested him as a guide, calling people to Him with insight and instructing them in tawhid and dhikr. The passage then states that one of Sanusi's great blessings was his companionship with this saint and his affiliation with him, and that other notable scholars also shared this bond, including his maternal brother Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tunisi, and Ahmad Zarruq. Finally, it begins a quotation from Ibn Maryam al-Militti about Sanusi taking from al-Tazi, but this is cut off. The passage emphasizes al-Tazi's role as a spiritual model and teacher.
