Sanusi's Sufi Initiation: The Khirqa
Sanusi's receipt of the khirqa from al-Tazi and its chain to Abu Madyan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Sufi khirqa in Sanusi's spiritual lineage and how he received it through a chain back to the great saint Abu Madyan.

Core Idea
The khirqa connects Sanusi to the spiritual authority of Abu Madyan.

The passage begins by recounting how Imam al-Sanusi received the Sufi cloak (khirqa) from Ibrahim al-Tazi, who himself has a chain to the famous saint Abu Madyan. This establishes Sanusi's credentials in the Sufi path.

Guided Path
1
Read the first section
Read the Arabic sentence about Ibrahim al-Tazi and the khirqa. Notice the chain from al-Tazi back to Abu Madyan.
The phrase 'ألبسه الخرقة' indicates the actual investiture.
2
Understand the significance of spitting
The passage mentions 'بصق في فيه' (spat in his mouth). This was a common act of transmitting blessing (baraka) among Sufi masters.
3
Reflect on the chain of transmission
Consider that the khirqa represents a spiritual lineage (silsila). By receiving it, Sanusi is linked to the illustrious Abu Madyan.
The chain strengthens his authority in both exoteric and esoteric sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران؛ ألبسه الخرقة، وحدَّثه بها عن شيو... وبصق في فيه، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ((١) والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير) الراشدي (٢)، ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها... الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي، شهر بأبركان، ومعناه بلسان البربرية: الأسود، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به، وكان يقول: (رأيت المشايخ والأولياء، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان (٣)، وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له: (جعلك الله الأئمة من المتقين)، قال العلامة ابن مريم: (فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته تبسم له، فيه ((٤) وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد... وضع يديه على رأسه وقال: نقرة خالصة!(٥) ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: (من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى، فليشدَّ عليه يده؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً) عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام: (وكأنه أشار لنفسه فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً ((١) وقال العلامة الشفشاوني: (وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد، ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأيلي، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح « البردة »، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح ) لامية ابن مالك »، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله ((٢)
Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he dressed him in the khirqa, and narrated to him from shaykhs... and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him ((1). And the arif al-Tazi had worn the khirqa according to the way of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and wore it from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi with his chain to Abu Madyan the famous arif and the great qutb) al-Rashidi (2). And among the noble souls to which the breaths of our Imam al-Sanusi were connected... the imam, the faqih, and the great qutb al-Hasan ibn Makhluf ibn Mas'ud al-Mazili, known as Abrakan, meaning in the Berber language: the black. He accompanied him much and benefited from him, and he used to say: 'I have seen shaykhs and awliya', but I have not seen anyone like my master al-Hasan Abrakan (3). When Imam al-Sanusi entered upon him and opened conversation with him, he said to him: 'May Allah make you among the imams of the pious.' The scholar Ibn Maryam said: 'So Allah realized his insight and his supplication; he smiled at him, in it ((4). In his childhood, when he passed with children by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure gold piece!' (5). And it appears that love of the Sufis had pervaded his heart, so he strove diligently for leadership in their path, and it is not a path of talk, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action. Therefore you find the complaint about the folding of its carpet, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the wonders in our time is that there exists a scholar for whom the knowledge of the outward and inward is gathered in the most perfect manner, such that one benefits from him in both sciences. The existence of someone like him is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. Let him hold fast to him, lest he lose him soon and find no one like him in east or west, ever.' Commenting on this statement, Shaykh al-Mallali, the student of the Imam, said: 'It is as if he pointed to himself, and he did not remain long after that until he was taken away, as if he revealed that to us. There is no doubt that no one like him will ever exist ((1). And the scholar al-Shafshawni said: 'His shaykhs and the shaykhs of Ibn Zakri are one. Among their shaykhs is the travelling scholar al-Ayli, with sukun of the lam, fath of the hamza, damm of the ya', and kasr of the lam. He is the first to introduce ilm al-kalam into the Maghreb in later times. And Shaykh Ibn Marzuq, commentator of al-Burda, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas, commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik, and Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zaghu, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Aqraqar, and Shaykh Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Jallab. My shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah informed me of that ((2).
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that presents several aspects of Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual lineage and reputation. It begins by mentioning Ibrahim al-Tazi, who invested Sanusi with the Sufi cloak (khirqa) and transmitted traditions to him, including the symbolic act of spitting into his mouth, a common practice of spiritual blessing. It then notes that al-Tazi himself received the khirqa through a chain from the famous saint Abu Madyan. Next, it highlights al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrakan, a great faqih and qutb whom Sanusi accompanied greatly. Sanusi's high regard for him is shown in his statement that he never saw anyone like him, and in the anecdote of Sanusi's supplication for him, which Ibn Maryam says was fulfilled. There is also a childhood story of Sanusi passing by Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, who placed his hands on his head and called him 'a pure gold piece', foretelling his future excellence. The passage then reflects on Sanusi's deep love for Sufism, emphasizing that the Sufi path is one of serious effort, not mere talk. It quotes Sanusi himself marveling at the rarity of a scholar who combines both exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) knowledge perfectly, and his warning to hold fast to such a person. His student al-Mallali interpreted this as Sanusi referring to himself, noting that he passed away soon after, as if disclosing his own uniqueness. Finally, al-Shafshawni provides a list of Sanusi's shaykhs, noting that one of them, al-Ayli, is credited with first introducing ilm al-kalam (theological philosophy) to the Maghreb in the later period. This biographical sketch thereby establishes Sanusi's credentials in both Sufism and academic scholarship.

The Scholar of Both Sciences: Sanusi and Abrakan
Sanusi's veneration of al-Hasan Abrakan and the prophecy of his own scholarly excellence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the value Sanusi placed on combining outward (zahir) and inward (batin) knowledge, as exemplified by his master al-Hasan Abrakan and a childhood prophecy.

Core Idea
Combining outward and inward knowledge is extremely rare and precious.

This part of the biography highlights Sanusi's deep admiration for al-Hasan Abrakan, who embodied both exoteric and esoteric sciences, and includes a childhood prophecy predicting Sanusi's future eminence.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Hasan Abrakan
Read the description of al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrakan. Note Sanusi's statement about never seeing anyone like him.
Abrakan means 'the black' in Berber.
2
Examine the childhood prophecy
Read the anecdote about Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid placing his hands on young Sanusi's head and calling him 'a pure gold piece'.
This foreshadows his future greatness.
3
Understand the union of sciences
Sanusi's quote about a scholar who combines both sciences perfectly and the comment by al-Mallali clarify that Sanusi himself was such a scholar.
The warning to hold fast to such a person underscores its rarity.

إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران؛ ألبسه الخرقة، وحدَّثه بها عن شيو... وبصق في فيه، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ((١) والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من شرف الدين الداعي، ولبسها من الشيخ صالح بن محمد الزواوي بسنده إلى أبي مدين العارف الشهير والقطب الكبير) الراشدي (٢)، ومن النفوس الشريفة التي اتصلت أنفاس إمامنا السنوسي بها... الإمام الفقيه والقطب الكبير الحسن بن مخلوف بن مسعود المزيلي، شهر بأبركان، ومعناه بلسان البربرية: الأسود، فلازمه كثيراً وانتفع به، وكان يقول: (رأيت المشايخ والأولياء، فما رأيت مثل سيدي الحسن أبركان (٣)، وكان إذا دخل عليه الإمام السنوسي وفاتحه بالكلام، وقال له: (جعلك الله الأئمة من المتقين)، قال العلامة ابن مريم: (فحقق الله فراسته ودعوته تبسم له، فيه ((٤) وفي صغره كان إذا مرَّ مع الصبيان على الإمام ابن مرزوق الحفيد... وضع يديه على رأسه وقال: نقرة خالصة!(٥) ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه: (من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى، فليشدَّ عليه يده؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً) عقب على هذه الكلمة الشيخ الملالي تلميذ الإمام: (وكأنه أشار لنفسه فلم يلبث بعده حتى خطف فكأنه كاشفنا بذلك، ولا شك أنه لا يوجد مثله أبداً ((١) وقال العلامة الشفشاوني: (وأشياخه وأشياخ ابن زكري واحد، ومن أشياخهما العالم الرحال الأيلي، بسكون اللام وفتح الهمزة وضم الياء وكسر اللام، وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب في الأزمنة المتأخرة، والشيخ ابن مرزوق شارح « البردة »، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن العباس شارح ) لامية ابن مالك »، والشيخ أبو العباس أحمد بن زاغ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله أقرقار، والشيخ أبو عثمان قاسم العقباني، والشيخ أبو عبد الله بن الجلاب، أفادني بذلك شيخنا أبو عبد الله محمد شقرون بن هبة الله ((٢)
Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Wahran; he dressed him in the khirqa, and narrated to him from shaykhs... and spat in his mouth, and narrated many things from him ((1). And the arif al-Tazi had worn the khirqa according to the way of the Sufi masters from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, and wore it from Shaykh Salih ibn Muhammad al-Zawawi with his chain to Abu Madyan the famous arif and the great qutb) al-Rashidi (2). And among the noble souls to which the breaths of our Imam al-Sanusi were connected... the imam, the faqih, and the great qutb al-Hasan ibn Makhluf ibn Mas'ud al-Mazili, known as Abrakan, meaning in the Berber language: the black. He accompanied him much and benefited from him, and he used to say: 'I have seen shaykhs and awliya', but I have not seen anyone like my master al-Hasan Abrakan (3). When Imam al-Sanusi entered upon him and opened conversation with him, he said to him: 'May Allah make you among the imams of the pious.' The scholar Ibn Maryam said: 'So Allah realized his insight and his supplication; he smiled at him, in it ((4). In his childhood, when he passed with children by Imam Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, he placed his hands on his head and said: 'A pure gold piece!' (5). And it appears that love of the Sufis had pervaded his heart, so he strove diligently for leadership in their path, and it is not a path of talk, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action. Therefore you find the complaint about the folding of its carpet, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the wonders in our time is that there exists a scholar for whom the knowledge of the outward and inward is gathered in the most perfect manner, such that one benefits from him in both sciences. The existence of someone like him is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. Let him hold fast to him, lest he lose him soon and find no one like him in east or west, ever.' Commenting on this statement, Shaykh al-Mallali, the student of the Imam, said: 'It is as if he pointed to himself, and he did not remain long after that until he was taken away, as if he revealed that to us. There is no doubt that no one like him will ever exist ((1). And the scholar al-Shafshawni said: 'His shaykhs and the shaykhs of Ibn Zakri are one. Among their shaykhs is the travelling scholar al-Ayli, with sukun of the lam, fath of the hamza, damm of the ya', and kasr of the lam. He is the first to introduce ilm al-kalam into the Maghreb in later times. And Shaykh Ibn Marzuq, commentator of al-Burda, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Abbas, commentator of the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik, and Shaykh Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Zaghu, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah Aqraqar, and Shaykh Abu Uthman Qasim al-Uqbani, and Shaykh Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Jallab. My shaykh Abu Abd Allah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah informed me of that ((2).
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that presents several aspects of Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual lineage and reputation. It begins by mentioning Ibrahim al-Tazi, who invested Sanusi with the Sufi cloak (khirqa) and transmitted traditions to him, including the symbolic act of spitting into his mouth, a common practice of spiritual blessing. It then notes that al-Tazi himself received the khirqa through a chain from the famous saint Abu Madyan. Next, it highlights al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrakan, a great faqih and qutb whom Sanusi accompanied greatly. Sanusi's high regard for him is shown in his statement that he never saw anyone like him, and in the anecdote of Sanusi's supplication for him, which Ibn Maryam says was fulfilled. There is also a childhood story of Sanusi passing by Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, who placed his hands on his head and called him 'a pure gold piece', foretelling his future excellence. The passage then reflects on Sanusi's deep love for Sufism, emphasizing that the Sufi path is one of serious effort, not mere talk. It quotes Sanusi himself marveling at the rarity of a scholar who combines both exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) knowledge perfectly, and his warning to hold fast to such a person. His student al-Mallali interpreted this as Sanusi referring to himself, noting that he passed away soon after, as if disclosing his own uniqueness. Finally, al-Shafshawni provides a list of Sanusi's shaykhs, noting that one of them, al-Ayli, is credited with first introducing ilm al-kalam (theological philosophy) to the Maghreb in the later period. This biographical sketch thereby establishes Sanusi's credentials in both Sufism and academic scholarship.

A) Al-Hasan Abrakan

Key Takeaway
Sanusi exemplified the rare combination of outward and inward knowledge, as recognized by his teachers and students.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that combining outward knowledge with inward spirituality is extremely rare. In your own journey of learning, have you prioritized your inner state as much as your external achievements? What one concrete change can you make this week to nurture your heart's connection to Allah alongside your studies?
?
Ibn Marzuq saw in the young Sanusi a 'pure silver coin' and prophesied his greatness. Do you believe that Allah has placed a unique potential within you, or do you live as if you are ordinary? How would your life change if you fully embraced that you are called to be a rare treasure? Commit to one way you will honor that calling starting today.
?
Sanusi's student recognized that his teacher was referring to himself when speaking of the rarity of the combined scholar. Are there gifts and insights that Allah has given you that you downplay or ignore? What would it mean for you to humbly acknowledge those gifts and use them for the sake of Allah, even if others do not see them?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
intermediate
5 min
Sanusi's Scholarly Network and the Introduction of Kalam
Enumeration of Sanusi's shaykhs and the claim that al-Ayli introduced ilm al-kalam to the Maghreb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the breadth of Sanusi's scholarly connections and the role of his shaykh al-Ayli in introducing ilm al-kalam to the Maghreb.

Core Idea
Al-Ayli brought ilm al-kalam to the Maghreb, and Sanusi studied with him.

The final part of the passage lists several of Sanusi's shaykhs and highlights one, al-Ayli, as the first to introduce ilm al-kalam (theological philosophy) to the Maghreb in later times. This cements Sanusi's credentials as a theologian.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of shaykhs
Read the list from al-Shafshawni, noting each name and their contributions (e.g., commentators of famous works).
The names include Ibn Marzuq and others.
2
Focus on al-Ayli
Identify al-Ayli and note his specific role: introducing ilm al-kalam to the Maghreb.
The phrase 'وهو أول من أدخل علم الكلام إلى المغرب' is key.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider that by having al-Ayli as a teacher, Sanusi was at the forefront of theological education in the region.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section that presents several aspects of Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual lineage and reputation. It begins by mentioning Ibrahim al-Tazi, who invested Sanusi with the Sufi cloak (khirqa) and transmitted traditions to him, including the symbolic act of spitting into his mouth, a common practice of spiritual blessing. It then notes that al-Tazi himself received the khirqa through a chain from the famous saint Abu Madyan. Next, it highlights al-Hasan ibn Makhluf al-Mazili, known as Abrakan, a great faqih and qutb whom Sanusi accompanied greatly. Sanusi's high regard for him is shown in his statement that he never saw anyone like him, and in the anecdote of Sanusi's supplication for him, which Ibn Maryam says was fulfilled. There is also a childhood story of Sanusi passing by Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid, who placed his hands on his head and called him 'a pure gold piece', foretelling his future excellence. The passage then reflects on Sanusi's deep love for Sufism, emphasizing that the Sufi path is one of serious effort, not mere talk. It quotes Sanusi himself marveling at the rarity of a scholar who combines both exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) knowledge perfectly, and his warning to hold fast to such a person. His student al-Mallali interpreted this as Sanusi referring to himself, noting that he passed away soon after, as if disclosing his own uniqueness. Finally, al-Shafshawni provides a list of Sanusi's shaykhs, noting that one of them, al-Ayli, is credited with first introducing ilm al-kalam (theological philosophy) to the Maghreb in the later period. This biographical sketch thereby establishes Sanusi's credentials in both Sufism and academic scholarship.

Al-Sanusi's Devotion to Sufism and the Rare Scholar
Sanusi's love for Sufism and his statement on the rarity of comprehensive scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Sanusi's deep commitment to Sufism and his view that true scholars master both exoteric and esoteric knowledge.

Core Idea
A true scholar combines external knowledge with internal spiritual realization.

This passage reveals Imam al-Sanusi's personal devotion to Sufism and his profound insight into the rarity of scholars who attain mastery of both the outward and inward sciences. His own statement about such a treasure reflects his self-awareness and the urgency of preserving such knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how al-Sanusi's love for Sufism is described as consuming his heart.
2
Analyze al-Sanusi's quote
Identify the key point: that a scholar who combines exoteric and esoteric knowledge is extremely rare and should be held onto.
He may be referring to himself.
3
Consider al-Mallali's comment
Note how al-Mallali interprets al-Sanusi's words as referring to himself, and confirms his uniqueness.
This shows the high esteem of his students.

ويظهر أنَّ محبة الصوفية قد تَبَلَتْ فؤادَهُ ، فسعى سعياً حثيثاً للريادة في طريقهم ، وهي ليست بطريقِ قال ، بل جد ومثابرة وفعال ، ولذا تجد الشكاية بطي بساطها ، حتى قال الإمام السنوسي نفسه : ( من الغرائب في زماننا هذا أن يوجد عالم جُمع له علم الظاهر والباطن على أكمل وجه ؛ بحيث يُنتفع به في العلمين ، فوجود مثله في غاية الندور ، فمن وجده فقد وجد كنزاً عظيماً دنيا وأخرى ، فليشدَّ عليه يده ؛ لئلا يضيع عن قرب فلا يجد مثله شرقاً وغرباً أبداً )

تلامذته
قال العلامة التنبكتي : ( أخذ عنه أعلام ؛ كابن صعد ، وأبي القاسم الزواوي ، وابن أبي مدين ، والشيخ يحيى بن محمد ، وابن الحاج البيدري ، وابن العباس الصغير ، وولي الله محمد القلعي ريحانة زمانه ، وإبراهيم الوجديجي ، وابن ملوكة ، وغيرهم من الفضلاء )

ومن جملة الأعلام الذين اجتمعوا به ، وحضروا عموم مجالسه دون
And it appears that love of Sufism had consumed his heart, so he strove earnestly to lead in their path, and it is not a path of saying, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action. Therefore you find complaint often spread, until Imam al-Sanusi himself said: 'Among the strange things in our time is that a scholar exists who has been granted the knowledge of the exoteric and the esoteric in the most complete manner, such that benefit is taken from him in both sciences. The existence of someone like him is extremely rare. Whoever finds him has found a great treasure in this world and the next. Let him hold fast to him, lest he be lost soon, and he never find his like in east or west forever.'
Al-Shaykh al-Mallali, the student of the Imam, commented on this statement: 'As if he pointed to himself, and it was not long after him that he was taken, as if he had revealed that to us, and there is no doubt that no one like him will ever exist.'
And al-"Allama al-Shafshawni said: 'His teachers and the teachers of Ibn Zakri are one. Among their teachers is the world-traveler al-Ayli — with sukun on the lam, fath on the hamza, damm on the ya', and kasr on the lam — and he is the first to introduce the science of kalam to the Maghreb in later times. And Shaykh Ibn Marzuq, commentator on al-Burda; and Shaykh Abu "Abd Allah ibn al-"Abbas, commentator on the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik; and Shaykh Abu al-"Abbas Ahmad ibn Zaghu; and Shaykh Abu "Abd Allah Aqraqar; and Shaykh Abu "Uthman Qasim al-"Uqbani; and Shaykh Abu "Abd Allah ibn al-Jallab. Our shaykh Abu "Abd Allah Muhammad Shaqrun ibn Hibat Allah informed me of that.'
His students:
Al-"Allama al-Tanbakti said: 'He was studied under by eminent scholars, such as Ibn Sa"d, Abu al-Qasim al-Zawawi, Ibn Abi Madin, Shaykh Yahya ibn Muhammad, Ibn al-Hajj al-Baydari, Ibn al-"Abbas al-Saghir, Wali Allah Muhammad al-Qal"i the fragrance of his time, Ibrahim al-Wujdiji, Ibn Muluka, and other virtuous ones.'
And al-Shaykh al-Mallali did not devote a chapter to discussing those who studied under the Imam, although he is one of the prominent students of the Imam, the historian of his life, and the compiler of his news and states.
And among those who studied under Imam al-Sanusi while being among his peers and the greats of his time was the Imam, the Shaykh, the gnostic of Allah most high, Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Barnusi al-Fasi, known as Zarruq, who died in the year 899 AH, despite his great station and high rank. He shared many of his teachers with al-Sanusi, and he himself stated that he studied under Imam al-Sanusi, as the historian al-"Allama al-Tanbakti narrated.
And among the eminent people who met him and attended his general gatherings...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a biographical passage providing details about Imam al-Sanusi's character, teachers, and students. It begins by noting his strong inclination towards Sufism, emphasizing that his pursuit was not merely theoretical but involved effort and action. A long quote from al-Sanusi is given where he laments the rarity of scholars who master both exoteric (zahir) and esoteric (batin) sciences, and advises holding fast to such a scholar if found. His student al-Mallali comments that al-Sanusi was likely referring to himself, and that no one like him would appear again.

Next, al-Shafshawni lists al-Sanusi's teachers, noting that they overlap with those of Ibn Zakri. He highlights al-Ayli as the first to introduce kalam to the Maghreb in later times, and names several other teachers including Ibn Marzuq (commentator on al-Burda) and Ibn al-Abbas (commentator on the Lamiyya of Ibn Malik).

Then al-Tanbakti lists al-Sanusi's students, mentioning several prominent scholars. The author notes that al-Mallali, though a student of al-Sanusi, did not write a section about those who studied under the Imam, even though he was a historian and collector of his biography.

Finally, the passage discusses Ahmad Zarruq, a famous scholar and contemporary of al-Sanusi, who also studied under him according to al-Tanbakti. It is noted that Zarruq shared many teachers with al-Sanusi, but was distinct in having traveled to Egypt and studied with scholars there. The passage ends mid-sentence on the page.

Key Terms
الصوفية
علم الظاهر
علم الباطن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Sanusi was exclusively a theologian and had no interest in Sufism.
Correction: The passage clearly states that love of Sufism had consumed his heart and he strived to lead in their path.

Checkpoint
What did al-Sanusi say about a scholar who combines both sciences?
A) They are common in the west.
B) They are extremely rare.
C) They are found in every generation.
D) They are not to be trusted.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's life exemplifies the integration of exoteric and esoteric knowledge, a rare combination he urged others to cherish.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sanusi said this rare scholar is a 'great treasure in this world and the next.' Who in your life—past or present—has been such a treasure to you? Have you truly valued them, or have you taken them for granted? What will you do this week to express your appreciation?
?
The path of Sufism is described as 'not of saying, but of seriousness, perseverance, and action.' Which of these three is most lacking in your own spiritual and academic pursuits? Name one concrete action you will take tomorrow to strengthen that quality.
?
If you were to come across a scholar like the one al-Sanusi described, would you hold fast to him, or would you let him slip away due to your own neglect? What practical step can you take right now to seek out such guidance in your community or through reliable sources?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

The Scholarly Network of Imam al-Sanusi: Teachers and Students
Lists al-Sanusi's teachers and students, highlighting their achievements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the key teachers and students of Imam al-Sanusi and understand their role in his intellectual development.

Core Idea
Knowledge is transmitted through chains of teachers and students spanning generations.

In this passage, we learn about the teachers who shaped al-Sanusi's education and the students who carried his legacy. The lists include notable figures who contributed to the spread of Islamic sciences in the Maghreb.

Guided Path
1
Read the lists of teachers and students
Notice the variety of scholars mentioned, including commentators and those who introduced kalam to the Maghreb.
2
Focus on al-Ayli
He is highlighted as the first to introduce kalam to the Maghreb in later times. Understand his significance.
3
Consider the student list
Many of the students became prominent scholars themselves, showing al-Sanusi's influence.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Imam al-Sanusi and Ahmad Zarruq: Peer and Student
Describes the mutual relationship between al-Sanusi and Ahmad Zarruq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique relationship between al-Sanusi and Ahmad Zarruq, where Zarruq was both a peer and a student of al-Sanusi.

Core Idea
Great scholars often learn from their contemporaries, showing humility and mutual respect.

This passage highlights the connection between al-Sanusi and the famous Sufi scholar Ahmad Zarruq. Despite being contemporaries and sharing teachers, Zarruq studied under al-Sanusi, illustrating the spirit of learning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Zarruq
Note that Zarruq is described as a peer and a student of al-Sanusi, and that he shared many teachers with him.
2
Consider the significance
This shows that even established scholars sought knowledge from each other, and al-Sanusi's reputation attracted students of high caliber.
3
Reflect on the chain of knowledge
The passage also mentions that Zarruq traveled to Egypt and studied with scholars there, indicating the wider network.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to learn from someone you consider your equal or even your junior? What pride or insecurity holds you back from acknowledging that they have knowledge you lack? Identify one peer whose knowledge you can seek this week.
?
Zarruq publicly acknowledged that he studied under al-Sanusi. Is there someone from whom you have learned but never publicly thanked or acknowledged? Write down their name and commit to expressing your gratitude to them before the week ends.
?
If you were in Zarruq's position—a respected scholar—would you have the humility to be a student of your contemporary? What would it cost you? What would it gain you? Be honest: is your desire for recognition stronger than your desire for truth?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Sanusi's Students and a Notable Encounter
Biographical account of Sanusi's students and al-Balawi's attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly circle of Imam Sanusi and how his 'Small Creed' was publicly recited.

Core Idea
Sanusi's legacy was upheld by students and even witnessed in public recitations.

This passage from a modern biographical source introduces us to some of Imam Sanusi's most prominent students and a unique eyewitness account. It shows how his works, especially the 'Small Creed', were not just scholarly texts but part of communal practice. We'll read about al-Balawi's experience attending Sanusi's mosque and hearing the creed recited from memory.

قال العلامة التنبكتي : ( أخذ عنه أعلام ؛ كابن صعد ، وأبي القاسم الزواوي ، وابن أبي مدين ، والشيخ يحيى بن محمد ، وابن الحاج البيدري ، وابن العباس الصغير ، وولي الله محمد القلعي ريحانة زمانه ، وإبراهيم الوجديجي ، وابن ملوكة ، وغيرهم من الفضلاء )(۱) ولم يعقد الشيخ الملالي باباً للحديث عن الآخذين عن الإمام ، وهو واحد من أعيان تلامذته ، والمؤرخ لسيرته ، ومجمع السنوسي أخباره وأحواله . وكان ممَّن تتلمذ للإمام السنوسي وهو من جملة أقرانه ، وأعيان أهل زمانه .. الإمام الشيخ العارف بالله تعالى أحمد بن أحمد البرنسي الفاسي المعروف بـ ( زروق ) ، والمتوفى سنة ( ٨٩٩هـ ) على جلالة شأنه وعلو قدره ، وقد شاركه في كثير من شيوخه ، وقد نص على التلمذة للإمام السنوسي بنفسه كما نقل ذلك المؤرخ العلامة التنبكتي (٢). ومن جملة الأعلام الذين اجتمعوا به ، وحضروا عموم مجالسه دون القراءة عليه مباشرةً : أبو جعفر أحمد بن علي البلوي الوادي آشي المتوفى سنة ( ٩٣٨ هـ ) ، وقد أرَّخَ له ولسيرته العطرة في « ثبته » المشهور ، ومن جملة ما قاله : ( لقيته رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وحضرت مجلسه الغاص بالمستفيدين من طلبة العلم والعامة بمسجده قرب داره بدرب مسوفة من داخل تلمسان أمَّنَها الله تعالى ، وحضرت  وأوائل سورة البقرة تقرأ عليه بالسبع ، وكتباً غير ذلك ؛ منها  ، كان يُقرأ عليه في بعض مجالس حضرتها ، ويتكلّم على أحاديثه بالكلام الذي يدلُّ على مقامه في العلم والعبادة وغيره من كُتب المجلس . وحضرنا - يومَ سلمنا عليه إثرَ ما صلينا العصر خلفه ـ « عقيدته الصغرى » تقرأ بين يديه ، يقرؤها طلبته وجمع من العوام الملازمين لمجلسه عن ظهر قلب سرداً على صوتٍ واحد إثر سلامِهِ من صلاة عصر يوم الجمعة عادة مستمرة ، وهو قاعد بمحرابه ، مقبل على الذكر )(۱) وحرصي على ذلك وقال : ( ولم تقدَّر لي القراءة عليه مع رغبتي في عليه ؛ لاستغراق طلبته أوقات قعوده ، حتى إنهم كانوا يقرؤون عليه والرملية في يد أحدهم إذا فرغت قطع ، وكنت أؤمل القراءة وأترصد لها وقتاً ، فعاجلته - قدَّسَهُ الله تعالى - المَنِيَّةُ ، ولم أنل من الأُمْنِيَّة )(۲)
Al-Tanbakti the scholar said: (Eminent figures took from him, such as Ibn Sa'd, Abu al-Qasim al-Zawawi, Ibn Abi Madin, Shaykh Yahya ibn Muhammad, Ibn al-Haj al-Baydari, Ibn al-Abbas al-Saghir, Wali Allah Muhammad al-Qal'i the fragrance of his time, Ibrahim al-Wujdiji, Ibn Maluka, and others of the virtuous.) (1) And Shaykh al-Mallali did not devote a chapter to discussing those who took from the Imam, while he is one of the prominent students, the historian of his biography, and the collector of Sanusi's news and circumstances. And among those who studied under Imam Sanusi while being among his peers and the prominent people of his time was the Imam, the scholar knower of Allah Almighty Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Barnisi al-Fasi known as (Zarruq), who died in the year (899 AH), despite his great status and high rank, and he shared many of his teachers with him, and he himself affirmed his study under Imam Sanusi as reported by the historian al-Tanbakti (2). And among the eminent figures who met him and attended his general gatherings without reading directly to him: Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashi, who died in the year (938 AH), and he recorded his biography and fragrant life in his famous 'Thabat', and among what he said: (I met him, may Allah be pleased with him, and attended his gathering crowded with beneficiaries from students of knowledge and the common people in his mosque near his house in Darb Masufa inside Tlemcen, may Allah protect it, and I attended the Fatiha and the beginnings of Surat al-Baqara being read to him in the seven modes, and other books; among them al-Bukhari, which was read to him in some gatherings I attended, and he commented on its hadiths with speech indicating his station in knowledge and worship and other books of the gathering. And we attended - the day we greeted him after we prayed Asr behind him - his 'Small Creed' being read before him, recited by his students and a group of common people attending his assembly from memory, chanting in one voice after his salutation from the Asr prayer on Friday, a continuous habit, while he sat in his prayer niche, engaged in remembrance.) (1) And my desire for that, and he said: (And I was not able to read to him despite my desire for it, because his students occupied all his sitting times, such that they would read to him and the sandglass was in the hand of one of them; when it ran out he would stop, and I hoped to read and waited for a time, but death hastened him - may Allah sanctify him - and I did not attain the wish.) (2)
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from a modern edition, likely from the book's introduction, describing the students and associates of Imam Sanusi. It begins by quoting al-Tanbakti, who lists notable scholars who studied under Sanusi: Ibn Sa'd, Abu al-Qasim al-Zawawi, Ibn Abi Madin, Shaykh Yahya ibn Muhammad, Ibn al-Haj al-Baydari, Ibn al-Abbas al-Saghir, Wali Allah Muhammad al-Qal'i, Ibrahim al-Wujdiji, Ibn Maluka, and others. The passage notes that al-Mallali, himself a prominent student and historian of Sanusi, did not dedicate a chapter to the list of students, implying a gap in the known sources. It then mentions that Zarruq, a famous scholar, studied under Sanusi despite being his peer. Finally, it gives a detailed account from al-Balawi, who attended Sanusi's lectures without being a direct student. Al-Balawi describes Sanusi's mosque gatherings, where the Qur'an was recited in multiple modes, al-Bukhari was read, and after Asr prayer on Fridays, Sanusi's 'Small Creed' was recited by students and commoners from memory. Al-Balawi laments that he could not read directly to Sanusi because students occupied all his time, and death prevented his wish.

The Teaching Circle of Imam Sanusi: Reciting the 'Aqida by Heart
Al-Balawi describes Sanusi's teaching session and the group recitation of his 'Aqida al-Sughra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional Islamic pedagogical practice of collective recitation from memory, as exemplified by Imam Sanusi's teaching circle.

Core Idea
Sanusi's students recited his creed from memory after prayer — faith integrated with worship.

This passage opens a window into the vibrant learning culture of 15th-century Tlemcen. Al-Balawi, a scholar visiting Sanusi's circle, describes how students and laypeople alike would recite the Imam's 'Small Creed' from memory after the Friday 'Asr prayer, with Sanusi himself engaged in dhikr. It shows that the study of 'aqida was not just intellectual but woven into the rhythm of daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Let the scene come to life: the crowded mosque, the recitation, the sand clock.
Notice the elements: Surat al-Fatiha, Surat al-Baqara in seven modes, Sahih al-Bukhari, and finally the 'Aqida al-Sughra.
2
Identify the key practice
The passage describes a regular Friday practice after 'Asr prayer. What exactly happened? Who participated? How did they recite?
The phrase 'عن ظهر قلب سرداً على صوت واحد' indicates unison recitation from memory.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is this practice notable? What does it tell us about the role of creed in daily life? How does it connect to the learning objective?
Consider that this was not just for scholars but for the general public (العوام).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القراءة عليه مباشرةً : أبو جعفر أحمد بن علي البلوي الوادي آشي المتوفى سنة ( ٩٣٨ هـ ) ، وقد أرَّخَ له ولسيرته العطرة في « ثبته » المشهور ، ومن جملة ما قاله : ( لقيته رضي الله تعالى عنه ، وحضرت مجلسه الغاص بالمستفيدين من طلبة العلم والعامة بمسجده قرب داره بدرب مسوفة من داخل تلمسان أمَّنَها الله تعالى ، وحضرت الفاتحة » وأوائل سورة البقرة » تقرأ عليه بالسبع ، وكتباً غير ذلك ؛ منها ( البخاري » ، كان يُقرأ عليه في بعض مجالس حضرتها ، ويتكلّم على أحاديثه بالكلام الذي يدلُّ على مقامه في العلم والعبادة وغيره من كُتب المجلس وحضرنا - يومَ سلمنا عليه إثرَ ما صلينا العصر خلفه ـ « عقيدته الصغرى » تقرأ بين يديه ، يقرؤها طلبته وجمع من العوام الملازمين لمجلسه عن ظهر قلب سرداً على صوتٍ واحد إثر سلامِهِ من صلاة عصر يوم الجمعة عادة مستمرة ، وهو قاعد بمحرابه ، مقبل على الذكر ((۱) وحرصي ذلك وقال : ( ولم تقدَّر لي القراءة عليه مع رغبتي في عليه ؛ لاستغراق طلبته أوقات قعوده ، حتى إنهم كانوا يقرؤون عليه والرملية في يد أحدهم إذا فرغت قطع ، وكنت أؤمل القراءة وأترصد لها وقتاً ، فعاجلته - قدَّسَهُ الله تعالى - المَنِيَّةُ ، ولم أنل من الأُمْنِيَّة ) (۲)
Direct reading upon him: Abu Ja'far Ahmad bin 'Ali al-Balawi al-Wadi Ashshi, died in the year (938 AH). He chronicled him and his fragrant biography in his famous 'Thabat'. Among what he said: (I met him - may God Most High be pleased with him - and attended his assembly crowded with beneficiaries from students of knowledge and the common people in his mosque near his house in Darb Masufa inside Tlemcen - may God protect it. And I attended 'al-Fatiha' and the beginnings of 'Surat al-Baqara' recited upon him in the seven modes, and other books; among them 'al-Bukhari', which was recited upon him in some sessions I attended, and he commented on its hadiths with speech indicating his station in knowledge and worship, and other books of the assembly. And we attended - on the day we greeted him after praying 'Asr behind him - his 'Small Creed' being recited before him. His students and a group of the common people who regularly attended his assembly recited it from memory, in a continuous chant on one voice after his greeting from the 'Asr prayer on Friday, a habitual practice, while he sat in his prayer niche, engaged in remembrance. (1) And my desire for that, and he said: (And I was not destined to read upon him despite my desire to do so, because his students occupied all his sitting times, so much so that they used to read upon him while the sand clock was in the hand of one of them; when it ran out, they would stop. And I hoped for reading and watched for a time, but death hastened him - may God sanctify him - and I did not attain the wish.) (2)
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from al-Balawi's 'Thabat' describing his experience attending the teaching sessions of Imam Sanusi. The passage begins by identifying al-Balawi and stating that he recorded Sanusi's biography. Then al-Balawi narrates his firsthand observations: he attended Sanusi's crowded assembly, which included both students and laypeople, in a mosque near Sanusi's house. He mentions that he heard the Fatiha and beginnings of Surat al-Baqara recited in the seven qira'at, and that Bukhari's Sahih was recited, with Sanusi commenting on the hadiths in a manner that revealed his deep knowledge and piety. A particularly vivid scene follows: after the 'Asr prayer on Friday, Sanusi's students and common people would recite his 'Small Creed' (al-'Aqida al-Sughra) from memory in unison, while Sanusi sat in his prayer niche engaged in dhikr. Al-Balawi then expresses his regret that he could not read directly upon Sanusi because the students constantly occupied his time, and he laments that Sanusi died before he could fulfill his wish.

Correction: The context shows it was a regular practice after prayer, reflecting deep integration of creed into worship, not mere repetition.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Sanusi's First Works: Al-Muqrib and Al-Aqida al-Kubra
Enumeration of Sanusi's early works with descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Sanusi's first two creedal works and their characteristics.

Core Idea
Sanusi's creedal journey began with an early commentary and a firm, difficult creed.

Imam al-Sanusi's theological output is vast, but his student al-Mallali focused on his creedal works. This lesson introduces the first two: his youthful commentary on al-Hawfi's Fara'id and his foundational creed, al-Aqida al-Kubra. These set the stage for his later masterpieces.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi
Notice the anecdote about his teacher's order to hide it until age forty. This shows Sanusi's early scholarly maturity.
2
Understand al-Aqida al-Kubra
Note that it is described as firm and difficult, indicating its depth. It was his first work in tawhid.
3
Review the commentary on al-Kubra
The commentary is one of his most extensive creedal books.

Source Text

مؤلفاته ومختلف العلمي
تنوعت تأليف الإمام السنوسي في المكتبة الإسلامية ، وهو واحد ممَّن أكثر من التأليف ، ورغم هذا التنوع كانت تأليفه العقدية تاج العلمي ، وقد عقد تلميذه الشيخ الملالي باباً خاصاً للحديث عنها ، وسترى بين يديك كل التآليف التي ذكرها ؛ وهي:

(1) « المقرب المستوفي في شرح فرائض الحوفي » : وهو أول مؤلفاته ، وكان عمره حين كتبه تسع عشرة أو ثماني عشرة سنة على اضطراب في ذلك ، وسيأتي خبره مع الشيخ العارف بالله الحسن أبركان وأمره له بإخفائه حتى يبلغ سن الأربعين (۲)

(۳) عقيدة أهل التوحيد » أو « العقيدة الكبرى (۳) : وهي أول ما صنف في علم التوحيد ، وعبارتها متينة مستصعبة كما نص في شرح العقيدة الوسطى (٤)

- عمدة أهل التوفيق والتسديد » أو «شرح العقيدة الكبرى » :
(۱) انظر ( المواهب القدسية » ( ق ١٠٢ )
(۲) انظر ( ص ٤٨ )
(۳) كذا كان يسميها الإمام السنوسي نفسه ، وانظر ( ص ١٥٥ ) ، أما الزيادة في عنوانها الأصلي : ( المخرجة من ظلمات الجهل وربقة التقليد . . . ) إلى آخره ، فهي وصف لها ، وليست جزءاً من اسمها كما يرى ذلك كل من العكاري والحامدي ، مع إثبات الملالي له
(٤) انظر ( شرح العقيدة الوسطى » ( ص ۱۲۳ ) .

وهذا الشرح يعدُّ من أوسع الكتب العقدية التي ألفها الإمام . ـ « العقيدة الوسطى » : وهي أخصـر مـن « الكبرى » وفوق الصغرى »

- شرح العقيدة الوسطى » : وهو من عيون ما ما أُلف في علم التوحيد .

- العقيدة الصغرى ( المعروفة بـ ( أم البراهين » و « ذات البراهين » و « السنوسية الصغرى » : وهي درَّةُ «عقائده » والمقصودة بقولهم : ( عقيدة السنوسي » عند الإطلاق ، وكتب لها من الذيوع ما لم يكتب لغيرها ، وأقبل عليها العلماء شرحاً ، والطلاب حفظاً ودرساً ، قال العلامة الملالي : ( وهي من أجل العقائد ، ولا تعادلها عقيدة من عقائد من تقدم ولا من تأخَّر من تقدم ولا من تأخر ، وقد أشار الشيخ رضي الله عنه إلى ذلك في صدر شرحه لها ((۱)

شرح العقيدة الصغرى » ، ويعرف أيضاً بـ « توحيد أهل العرفان ومعرفة الله ورسله بالدليل والبرهان » ، وبـ « شرح أم البراهين » وهو أيضاً قد كتب له الذيوع والانتشار في الآفاق ، وكم من حاشية وضعت عليه

صغرى الصغرى ((۲) : وصفها الشيخ الملالي بقوله :
(۱) انظر » المواهب القدسية » ( ق ١٠٣ )
(۲) وقد تُسمَّى أحياناً : « العقيدة الوجيزة ) ، وبذا تسمَّى أيضاً : «صغرى صغرى الصغرى » كما سترى .
His writings and various sciences. The works of Imam al-Sanusi diversified in the Islamic library, and he is one of those who authored prolifically. Despite this diversity, his creedal works were the crown of his sciences. His student, Shaykh al-Mallali, devoted a special chapter to discuss them, and you will see before you all the works he mentioned; they are:

(1) 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi fi Sharh Fara'id al-Hawfi': This is his first work. He wrote it at the age of nineteen or eighteen, with some uncertainty about that. His story with the gnostic Shaykh al-Hasan Abarkan and his order to hide it until he reached forty will come.

(3) 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' or 'al-Aqida al-Kubra' (3): This is the first work he composed in the science of tawhid. Its phrasing is firm and difficult, as stated in his commentary on 'al-Aqida al-Wusta' (4).

- 'Umdat Ahl al-Tawfiq wa al-Tasdid' or 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra':
(1) See 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (folio 102).
(2) See p. 48.
(3) Thus Imam al-Sanusi himself would name it. See p. 155. As for the addition to its original title: 'al-Mukharraja min Zulumat al-Jahl wa Rabqat al-Taqlid...' etc., it is a description of it, not part of its name, as both al-Ukkari and al-Hamidi hold, with al-Mallali confirming it.
(4) See 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta' (p. 123).

And this commentary is considered among the most extensive creedal books authored by the Imam.
- 'al-Aqida al-Wusta': It is shorter than 'al-Kubra' and above 'al-Sughra'.

- 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta': It is among the masterpieces composed in the science of tawhid.

- 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (known as 'Umm al-Barahin', 'Dhat al-Barahin', and 'al-Sanusiyya al-Sughra'): It is the pearl of his creeds and the intended meaning when they say 'Aqidat al-Sanusi' in an absolute sense. It achieved a renown that no other creed achieved. Scholars engaged with it through commentaries, and students through memorization and study. The scholar al-Mallali said: 'It is among the greatest creeds; no creed from those who preceded or followed equals it. The Shaykh, may God be pleased with him, alluded to this in the opening of his commentary on it.'

>>
'Sharh al-Aqida al-Sughra', also known as 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan wa Ma'rifat Allah wa Rusulihi bi al-Dalil wa al-Burhan', and 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'. It too achieved renown and spread across horizons, and how many glosses have been written upon it.

'Sughra al-Sughra' ((2): al-Mallali described it by saying:
(1) See 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (folio 103).
(2) It is sometimes called 'al-Aqida al-Wajiza', and thus also called 'Sughra Sughra al-Sughra' as you will see.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a biographical catalog of Imam al-Sanusi's major theological works. It begins by noting that although Sanusi authored in many fields, his creedal works are paramount. His student al-Mallali collected them. The first work listed is 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi', a commentary on al-Hawfi's Fara'id, written in his youth. Next is 'al-Aqida al-Kubra', his first creed, described as firm (matin) and difficult (mustas'aba). Then its commentary 'Umdat Ahl al-Tawfiq'. Then 'al-Aqida al-Wusta', intermediate in size, and its commentary. Then the renowned 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (Umm al-Barahin), which the author says is unequaled. Then its commentary. Finally, 'Sughra al-Sughra', an even smaller creed. The passage emphasizes the fame and wide acceptance of the Sughra, quoting al-Mallali's praise. The inclusion of footnote references (e.g., to al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya) indicates scholarly documentation.

Key Terms
المقرب المستوفي
العقيدة الكبرى
شرح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Aqida al-Kubra is Sanusi's most famous creed.
Correction: While it is his first, the passage indicates that al-Aqida al-Sughra later achieved greater fame.

Checkpoint
What is unique about Sanusi's first work, al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi?
A) It is a commentary on a work by al-Hawfi.
B) It was written when he was over forty.
C) It is a creedal work.
D) It is the most famous of his works.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's early creedal works, including a youthful commentary and his first creed, laid the foundation for his later theological contributions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi wrote his first work at 18 or 19. What are you building in your youth that will serve your faith and knowledge? If nothing, what is holding you back?
?
His teacher told him to hide his work until age 40. Do you have the patience and trust to wait for wisdom before displaying your efforts? Where in your life are you rushing to show what you have not yet matured?
?
Al-Aqida al-Kubra is described as 'firm and difficult'. Does your understanding of tawhid have that firmness? Where do you compromise or settle for ease in matters of belief?

The Intermediate Creed: Al-Aqida al-Wusta and Its Commentary
Brief description of al-Aqida al-Wusta and its commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of al-Aqida al-Wusta among Sanusi's creeds and the significance of its commentary.

Core Idea
The middle creed balances conciseness and depth.

After the extensive al-Kubra, Sanusi composed a shorter creed, al-Aqida al-Wusta, which sits between the large and small creeds. Its commentary is considered a masterpiece of tawhid. This lesson explores these intermediate works.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of al-Aqida al-Wusta
Note that it is shorter than al-Kubra but above al-Sughra.
2
Understand its commentary
The commentary is praised as among the best works in tawhid.
3
Reflect on the progression
Think about why Sanusi might have written multiple creeds of varying lengths.

Source Text

مؤلفاته ومختلف العلمي
تنوعت تأليف الإمام السنوسي في المكتبة الإسلامية ، وهو واحد ممَّن أكثر من التأليف ، ورغم هذا التنوع كانت تأليفه العقدية تاج العلمي ، وقد عقد تلميذه الشيخ الملالي باباً خاصاً للحديث عنها ، وسترى بين يديك كل التآليف التي ذكرها ؛ وهي:

(1) « المقرب المستوفي في شرح فرائض الحوفي » : وهو أول مؤلفاته ، وكان عمره حين كتبه تسع عشرة أو ثماني عشرة سنة على اضطراب في ذلك ، وسيأتي خبره مع الشيخ العارف بالله الحسن أبركان وأمره له بإخفائه حتى يبلغ سن الأربعين (۲)

(۳) عقيدة أهل التوحيد » أو « العقيدة الكبرى (۳) : وهي أول ما صنف في علم التوحيد ، وعبارتها متينة مستصعبة كما نص في شرح العقيدة الوسطى (٤)

- عمدة أهل التوفيق والتسديد » أو «شرح العقيدة الكبرى » :
(۱) انظر ( المواهب القدسية » ( ق ١٠٢ )
(۲) انظر ( ص ٤٨ )
(۳) كذا كان يسميها الإمام السنوسي نفسه ، وانظر ( ص ١٥٥ ) ، أما الزيادة في عنوانها الأصلي : ( المخرجة من ظلمات الجهل وربقة التقليد . . . ) إلى آخره ، فهي وصف لها ، وليست جزءاً من اسمها كما يرى ذلك كل من العكاري والحامدي ، مع إثبات الملالي له
(٤) انظر ( شرح العقيدة الوسطى » ( ص ۱۲۳ ) .

وهذا الشرح يعدُّ من أوسع الكتب العقدية التي ألفها الإمام . ـ « العقيدة الوسطى » : وهي أخصـر مـن « الكبرى » وفوق الصغرى »

- شرح العقيدة الوسطى » : وهو من عيون ما ما أُلف في علم التوحيد .

- العقيدة الصغرى ( المعروفة بـ ( أم البراهين » و « ذات البراهين » و « السنوسية الصغرى » : وهي درَّةُ «عقائده » والمقصودة بقولهم : ( عقيدة السنوسي » عند الإطلاق ، وكتب لها من الذيوع ما لم يكتب لغيرها ، وأقبل عليها العلماء شرحاً ، والطلاب حفظاً ودرساً ، قال العلامة الملالي : ( وهي من أجل العقائد ، ولا تعادلها عقيدة من عقائد من تقدم ولا من تأخَّر من تقدم ولا من تأخر ، وقد أشار الشيخ رضي الله عنه إلى ذلك في صدر شرحه لها ((۱)

>>
شرح العقيدة الصغرى » ، ويعرف أيضاً بـ « توحيد أهل العرفان ومعرفة الله ورسله بالدليل والبرهان » ، وبـ « شرح أم البراهين » وهو أيضاً قد كتب له الذيوع والانتشار في الآفاق ، وكم من حاشية وضعت عليه

صغرى الصغرى ((۲) : وصفها الشيخ الملالي بقوله :
(۱) انظر » المواهب القدسية » ( ق ١٠٣ )
(۲) وقد تُسمَّى أحياناً : « العقيدة الوجيزة ) ، وبذا تسمَّى أيضاً : «صغرى صغرى الصغرى » كما سترى .
His writings and various sciences. The works of Imam al-Sanusi diversified in the Islamic library, and he is one of those who authored prolifically. Despite this diversity, his creedal works were the crown of his sciences. His student, Shaykh al-Mallali, devoted a special chapter to discuss them, and you will see before you all the works he mentioned; they are:

(1) 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi fi Sharh Fara'id al-Hawfi': This is his first work. He wrote it at the age of nineteen or eighteen, with some uncertainty about that. His story with the gnostic Shaykh al-Hasan Abarkan and his order to hide it until he reached forty will come.

(3) 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid' or 'al-Aqida al-Kubra' (3): This is the first work he composed in the science of tawhid. Its phrasing is firm and difficult, as stated in his commentary on 'al-Aqida al-Wusta' (4).

- 'Umdat Ahl al-Tawfiq wa al-Tasdid' or 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra':
(1) See 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (folio 102).
(2) See p. 48.
(3) Thus Imam al-Sanusi himself would name it. See p. 155. As for the addition to its original title: 'al-Mukharraja min Zulumat al-Jahl wa Rabqat al-Taqlid...' etc., it is a description of it, not part of its name, as both al-Ukkari and al-Hamidi hold, with al-Mallali confirming it.
(4) See 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta' (p. 123).

And this commentary is considered among the most extensive creedal books authored by the Imam.
- 'al-Aqida al-Wusta': It is shorter than 'al-Kubra' and above 'al-Sughra'.

- 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Wusta': It is among the masterpieces composed in the science of tawhid.

- 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (known as 'Umm al-Barahin', 'Dhat al-Barahin', and 'al-Sanusiyya al-Sughra'): It is the pearl of his creeds and the intended meaning when they say 'Aqidat al-Sanusi' in an absolute sense. It achieved a renown that no other creed achieved. Scholars engaged with it through commentaries, and students through memorization and study. The scholar al-Mallali said: 'It is among the greatest creeds; no creed from those who preceded or followed equals it. The Shaykh, may God be pleased with him, alluded to this in the opening of his commentary on it.'

>>
'Sharh al-Aqida al-Sughra', also known as 'Tawhid Ahl al-Irfan wa Ma'rifat Allah wa Rusulihi bi al-Dalil wa al-Burhan', and 'Sharh Umm al-Barahin'. It too achieved renown and spread across horizons, and how many glosses have been written upon it.

'Sughra al-Sughra' ((2): al-Mallali described it by saying:
(1) See 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' (folio 103).
(2) It is sometimes called 'al-Aqida al-Wajiza', and thus also called 'Sughra Sughra al-Sughra' as you will see.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a biographical catalog of Imam al-Sanusi's major theological works. It begins by noting that although Sanusi authored in many fields, his creedal works are paramount. His student al-Mallali collected them. The first work listed is 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi', a commentary on al-Hawfi's Fara'id, written in his youth. Then 'al-Aqida al-Wusta', intermediate in size, and its commentary. Then the renowned 'al-Aqida al-Sughra' (Umm al-Barahin), which the author says is unequaled. Then its commentary. Finally, 'Sughra al-Sughra', an even smaller creed. The passage emphasizes the fame and wide acceptance of the Sughra, quoting al-Mallali's praise. The Cornerstone Creed: Al-Aqida al-Sughra (Umm al-Barahin)
Detailed description of al-Aqida al-Sughra and its related works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Aqida al-Sughra is Sanusi's most famous creed and appreciate its widespread acceptance.

Core Idea
The small creed that became the most celebrated.

Of all Sanusi's creeds, al-Aqida al-Sughra, commonly known as Umm al-Barahin, achieved unparalleled renown. Scholars and students alike have engaged with it extensively. This lesson covers this work, its commentary, and the even smaller Sughra al-Sughra.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Aqida al-Sughra
Note that it is called the pearl of his creeds and the default meaning of 'Aqidat al-Sanusi'.
2
Understand its fame
It achieved a renown no other creed achieved, with many commentaries and studies.
3
Consider the commentary and Sughra al-Sughra
The commentary also spread widely, and an even smaller version exists.

The Diverse Scholarship of Imam al-Sanusi: A Catalogue of Works
A list of Sanusi's works with brief descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wide range of Islamic sciences that Imam al-Sanusi contributed to, including hadith, fiqh, tafsir, logic, and mathematics, as evidenced by his major writings.

Core Idea
Sanusi's pen touched every major Islamic science.

This passage provides a rare glimpse into the expansive scholarly output of Imam al-Sanusi. While he is renowned for his foundational works in theology (kalam), this list reveals his mastery of hadith, logic, and even algebra. Let us examine these entries to appreciate the depth and breadth of his intellectual legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read through the Arabic text and its translation. Note the variety of subjects mentioned: hadith, logic, mathematics, and theology.
Pay attention to the names of the works and their descriptions.
2
Categorize the works by subject
Group the works into categories such as hadith (commentaries on Bukhari and Muslim), logic (Isaghuji, Jumal), and others (algebra, theology).
This helps see Sanusi's range at a glance.
3
Identify unfinished works
Note which works are described as incomplete or only seen in manuscript. For example, his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari was not completed.
This shows Sanusi's active scholarly life.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider what this list tells us about Sanusi's role as a scholar and teacher. He was not only a theologian but a polymath.

This poem in explanation of al-Jazairiyyah: it is an explanation of the poem of Imam al-Faqih Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abdillah al-Jazairi, and Imam al-Sanusi described the beginning of his book by saying: (It is a poem containing both ways of guidance for the elite and commoners), and it is a lamia poem in the basit meter, and it is also known as al-Jazairiyyah in the Islamic creeds. And the author of the poem is the one who requested Imam al-Sanusi to explain it. And al-Alawi said: (It is a precious poem that was sent to him from Algeria to explain it, so he wrote this noble explanation, which is large and full of benefits in various sciences). (1)
Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal by Imam al-Ubbi: it is an explanation of Sahih Imam Muslim. Shaykh al-Malali said: (He added in it strange points and wonderful pearls, and it is in two large volumes). (2)
- Explanation of Sahih Imam al-Bukhari: Shaykh al-Malali said: (He did not complete it), and he mentioned that he reached the chapter of 'Whoever sought to make his religion free from doubts'. (3)
- Explanation of Problematic Hadiths of Sahih al-Bukhari: These similar hadiths occurred at its end, and they are problematic for one of weak understanding and feeble expression.

(1) See: Thabit Abi Ja'far al-Balawi (p. 441) (2) See: al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah (fol. 104), and al-Imam al-Allamah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi and his Efforts in Service of the Noble Prophetic Hadith by Prof. Dr. Abd al-Aziz Dakhan (3) See: al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah (fol. 106).

- Explanation of al-Yasminiyyah: Shaykh al-Malali said: (Among them is his explanation that he wrote on the Introduction to Algebra by Abu Muhammad Abdallah ibn Hajjaj known as Ibn al-Yasmin, and he wrote this explanation in his youth, and I saw it in his handwriting). (2)
- Explanation of al-Khunji's Jumal on logic: Likely he did not complete it. al-Malali said: (I saw notebooks of it). (3)
- Explanation of Isaghuji on logic: Shaykh al-Malali said: (It is by Abu al-Hasan Ibrahim ibn Umar ibn al-Hasan al-Rabbat ibn Ali ibn Abi [Bakr] al-Biqa'i al-Shafi'i, and it is a large-bodied explanation, abundant in knowledge). (4)
-
Explanation of the abridgement of Imam Ibn Arafa al-Warghami on logic: He solved in it what was difficult from the expression of Imam Ibn Arafa. Shaykh al-Malali said: (And the shaykh, may Allah be pleased with him, told me: Ibn Arafa's speech is very difficult).
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical list of the works of Imam Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi. It begins with a commentary on the al-Jazairiyyah poem, explaining that the poem was written by Ahmad al-Jazairi and sent to Sanusi from Algeria for commentary. Sanusi described the poem as containing guidance for both elites and commoners. The commentary is described as large and full of benefits. Next, the Mukammil Ikmal al-Ikmal by al-Ubbi is an explanation of Sahih Muslim, praised by al-Malali for its rare points. Then comes an unfinished commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari, which stopped at a specific chapter, and a work on problematic hadiths of Sahih al-Bukhari. After a footnote reference, the list continues with an abridgement of al-Zarkashi's commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari, seen in Sanusi's hand, and an abridgement of al-Taftazani's gloss on al-Kashshaf, noted as incomplete. The next item is a commentary on al-Yasminiyyah (on algebra), written in Sanusi's youth. Then a commentary on al-Khunji's Jumal on logic, possibly incomplete, and a commentary on Isaghuji on logic by al-Biqa'i, described as large and knowledgeable. Finally, a commentary on Ibn Arafa's Mukhtasar on logic, where Sanusi clarified difficult passages, with al-Malali reporting Ibn Arafa's speech as very difficult. This list shows Sanusi's breadth in fiqh, hadith, tafsir, logic, and mathematics.

Sanusi's Major Works and Their Commentaries
Al-Mallali enumerates Sanusi's works and describes each commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be familiar with four key works of Imam Sanusi and the nature of their commentaries as recorded by Al-Mallali.

Core Idea
Al-Mallali's list gives us a glimpse of Sanusi's scholarly output and his influences.

This passage is not a theological argument but a bibliographical note. Al-Shaykh al-Mallali, a later scholar, lists four works by Imam al-Sanusi, each with a brief observation about its completion or method. By studying this list, we gain insight into Sanusi's areas of focus: creed, grammar, kalam, and tafsir, as well as his engagement with earlier scholars like al-Baydawi and al-Adud al-Iji.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the pattern: each work is named and followed by a comment.
The passage is a list, so read it as a catalogue.
2
Identify each work and its description
Locate the four works: Sharh al-Aqida al-Murshida, al-Durr al-Manzum, Sharh Jawahir al-Ulum, and Tafsir al-Qur'an al-Aziz. Note what al-Mallali says about each.
3
Note the special remark on Sharh Jawahir al-Ulum
This commentary is highlighted as difficult, with Sanusi's own remark about al-Baydawi being the 'point' of the book. Consider what this tells us about Sanusi's intellectual method.
Al-Baydawi's Tawali' al-Anwar was a major kalam work.
4
Consider the incomplete tafsir
The tafsir stops at verse 5 of Surat al-Baqara. Reflect on why a scholar might leave a tafsir unfinished, and what this implies about his priorities.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح العقيدة المرشدة » : قال الشيخ الملالي : ( رأيته مكملاً بخطه )

Explanation of the Guiding Creed: Al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: (I saw it complete in his handwriting). The Scattered Pearls in Explaining the Rules of Ibn Ajrum: It is an explanation of al-Ajurumiyya in the science of grammar, in the science of grammar, al-Shaykh al-Mallali said: (I saw it in his handwriting, complete). Explanation of the Jewels of the Sciences (in the science of kalam): The original is by al-Allama al-Adud al-Iji, and it is on the method of Imam al-Baydawi in his 'Tawali' al-Anwar'; indeed, its difficulty reached such an extent that al-Shaykh al-Imam al-Sanusi said: (Al-Baydawi is the point of this book). Interpretation of the Mighty Quran: He reached in it to the saying of the Most High from Surat al-Baqara: 'Those are upon guidance from their Lord, and those are the successful ones' [al-Baqara: 5].
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a biographical-bibliographical enumeration. Al-Shaykh al-Mallali lists four of Imam al-Sanusi's works with brief annotations. First, 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Murshida' is noted as seen complete in Sanusi's own handwriting. Second, 'al-Durr al-Manzum fi Sharh Qawa'id Ibn Ajrum' is a grammar commentary on the famous Ajurumiyya text, also confirmed in Sanusi's hand. Third, 'Sharh Jawahir al-Ulum' is a work on kalam; its original author is al-Adud al-Iji, and it follows the methodology of al-Baydawi's 'Tawali' al-Anwar'. Al-Sanusi remarked on its difficulty, likening al-Baydawi's role to the foundational point of the work. Fourth, 'Tafsir al-Qur'an al-Aziz' is an unfinished commentary reaching verse 5 of Surat al-Baqara.

Beyond the Books: Sanusi's Diverse Writings
Al-Mallali enumerates Sanusi's miscellaneous writings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the range of a classical scholar's intellectual output, including fatwas, sermons, letters, and even amulets, as exemplified by Imam al-Sanusi.

Core Idea
A scholar's legacy includes not only books but also letters, sermons, and even amulets.

Al-Mallali, after listing al-Sanusi's major authored works, adds a crucial note: the scholar's output extended far beyond formal books. He wrote answers to queries, sermons, bequests, letters, and even amulets requested by people. This lesson explores that broader legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp the full list of writings.
The passage is a continuous quotation from al-Mallali.
2
Identify the six categories mentioned
List each type of writing al-Mallali adds: answers, sermons, bequests, letters, amulets, and handwritten copies.
Some answers are considered independent works.
3
Reflect on the significance of answers
Notice that al-Mallali says some answers are long and independent enough to be counted as authored works. What does that say about Sanusi's scholarly engagement?
This shows responsiveness to community needs.
4
Consider the inclusion of amulets (hujub)
Think about why a scholar would write amulets. What role did this serve in his society?
It reflects the practical, spiritual role of scholars.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ العلامة الملالي المؤرخ لسيرة الإمام السنوسي بعدما أورد جميع هذه التصانيف : ( فهذا ما علمنا الله من تأليفه رضي عنه ، وزد مع ذلك : ما كتبه من الأجوبة على المسائل التي ترد عليه في جلّ الأوقات ، وبعض الأجوبة يحسن أن تعدها من تأليفه رضي الله عنه ؛ لكبرها واستقلالها بنفسها ، وما كتب من المواعظ والوصايا والرسائل والحُجُب التي يطلب فيها ، وما نسخ بيده من تصانيف العلماء ودواوين القدماء )
Al-Shaykh al-Allama al-Mallali, the historian of the biography of Imam al-Sanusi, after presenting all these works, said: (This is what we know of his composition, may Allah be pleased with him. Add to that: what he wrote of answers to questions that came to him in most times, and some answers may be counted as his composition, may Allah be pleased with him, due to their length and independence, and what he wrote of sermons, bequests, letters, and amulets that were requested of him, and what he copied by hand of the works of scholars and the diwans of the ancients.)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a supplementary biographical note by al-Mallali. After listing Sanusi's major authored works, al-Mallali adds that Sanusi also produced responses to legal and theological queries, some of which are substantial enough to be considered independent treatises. Additionally, he wrote sermons, wills, letters, and talismans (hujub) requested by others. He also made handwritten copies of other scholars' works and classical poetry collections. This demonstrates Sanusi's wide-ranging scholarly activity beyond formal book authorship.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Scholars only produce formal authored books.
Correction: In addition to books, scholars write responses, sermons, letters, and even amulets, as seen in al-Sanusi's output.

Scholarly Praise for al-Sanusi's Authority and Virtue
Quotes scholars praising al-Sanusi's flawless writings and virtuous character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how external scholarly testimony and direct description establish al-Sanusi's authority in both knowledge and character.

Core Idea
Al-Sanusi's works were deemed flawless and his character saintly.

Before delving into al-Sanusi's theological arguments, it is essential to appreciate the reverent context in which his works were received. In this passage, the author cites two prominent scholars who attest to the perfection of al-Sanusi's writings and his virtuous character, reinforcing why his texts became foundational in Ash'ari kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the two scholarly testimonies
Read the quotes from al-Shifshāwnī and al-Habṭī. Notice how they emphasize perfection and preservation from error.
The first quote is from al-Shifshāwnī; the second from al-Habṭī.
2
Identify the key descriptors
Look for phrases like 'تنوير كلامه' (illumination of his speech) and 'محفوظ من السقطات' (preserved from slips).
3
Analyze the character description
Read the author's own description of al-Sanusi's character. Note the list of virtues: خير، بر، تقي، ورع، زاهد، حليم، صبور.
These are traits of a saintly scholar.
4
Reflect on the overall purpose
Consider why the author includes these praises at the outset. They establish his credibility and the esteem in which he is held.
This is a common feature in Islamic scholarly works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد وصف الشفشاوني تأليف الإمام السنوسي بكلمة جامعة فقال : ( ناهيك بتنوير كلامه ، وإتقان عبارته ، حتى لا يجد المتعسف مدخلاً للتعقب بوجه ولا بحال ، واتفاقِ فحول الأولياء وأكابر العلماء على فضله وتلقي تآليفه بالقبول ((۱)
ونقل عن الإمام أبي عبد الله الهبطي قوله : ( كلام السنوسي
محفوظ من السقطات )(۲)
.
قبس من عظیم اخلاق
الله تعالى للإمام السنوسي إلى عظيم علمه وبحبوحة
معرفتِه . . سعة الأخلاق الحميدة ، فجابَ شُعب الإيمان وطنَّبَ فيها خيامه ، فعُهِدَ عنه أنه خيرٌ برٌّ ، تقي ورع زاهد ، حليم صبور .
(۱) انظر ( دوحة الناشر » ( ص ١٢١ )
(۲) انظر ( دوحة الناشر » ( ص ١٢٢ )
Al-Shifshāwnī described the writings of Imam al-Sanusi with a comprehensive statement, saying: 'Sufficient is the illumination of his speech, the perfection of his expression, so that the unjustified critic finds no entrance to object in any way or in any situation, and the agreement of the foremost saints and senior scholars on his virtue and the acceptance of his works.' (1) And he transmitted from Imam Abū ʿAbd Allāh al-Habṭī his statement: 'The speech of al-Sanusi is preserved from slips.' (2) A spark from the great morals [of?] God – exalted be He – for Imam al-Sanusi, in addition to his great knowledge and vastness of his understanding ... the breadth of praiseworthy morals. He traversed the branches of faith and pitched his tents within them. It was known about him that he was good, pious, God-fearing, ascetic, forbearing, patient. (1) See 'Dawḥat al-Nāshir' (p. 121). (2) See 'Dawḥat al-Nāshir' (p. 122).
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents praise for Imam al-Sanusi's writings and character from two scholars. First, al-Shifshāwnī offers a comprehensive assessment: al-Sanusi's speech is illuminated (tanwīr kalāmihi) and his expression perfected (itqān ʿibāratihi), leaving no room for unjustified criticism (al-mutaʿassif). Moreover, the leading saints (fuḥūl al-awliyāʾ) and senior scholars (akābir al-ʿulamāʾ) unanimously acknowledge his virtue and accept his works (talqī taʾālīfihi bi-l-qabūl). Second, al-Habṭī states that al-Sanusi's speech is preserved from slips (maḥfūẓ min al-saqaṭāt), implying doctrinal and linguistic infallibility in his writings. The author then adds a personal description of al-Sanusi's character: he was good (khayr), pious (barr), God-fearing (taqī), ascetic (zāhid), forbearing (ḥalīm), and patient (ṣabūr). The metaphor of traversing the branches of faith (jāba shuʿab al-īmān) and pitching tents within them suggests his deep engagement with all aspects of religious life. The passage thus combines external scholarly testimony with direct character commendation.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanusi's writings were universally praised for perfection, and his personal character exemplified the highest virtues.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sanusi's character was described as 'good, pious, God-fearing, ascetic, forbearing, patient.' Which of these qualities do you lack most in your daily life, and what one concrete step will you take this week to cultivate it?
?
The scholars unanimously accepted al-Sanusi's works. Is there a point of Islamic belief or practice that you have doubted or rejected because of a personal opinion? Are you willing to submit to the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna, even if it contradicts your own inclination?
?
Al-Sanusi's speech was 'preserved from slips.' When you speak about Allah, His Messenger, or the religion, do you guard your tongue from ignorance, exaggeration, or carelessness? Will you commit to checking your words against the Qur'an and Sunna before speaking?

Scholars' Testimony on al-Sanusi's Works
Two scholars praise al-Sanusi's writings.

Learning Objective

Al-Sanusi's works are so precise that critics can find no fault.

Before studying the theological arguments of al-Sanusi, it is valuable to know how his peers regarded his works. Two renowned scholars provide succinct testimonies that establish the reliability and authority of his writings. Their words remind us that these texts have been scrutinized and endorsed by the scholarly community.

Guided Path

Commentary
This passage is a collection of two testimonies from notable scholars praising Imam al-Sanusi's written works. Moreover, the leading saints and scholars agree on his excellence and accept his writings. The second testimony is from al-Habtī, who states that al-Sanusi's speech is protected from errors or slips, implying divine safeguarding of his scholarly output. These quotes establish al-Sanusi's high standing in the eyes of his contemporaries.

The Noble Character of Imam al-Sanusi
Biographical description of al-Sanusi's ethical and devotional qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key virtues and devotional practices that defined Imam al-Sanusi's character, as described by his biographer.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's character was a living reflection of divine attributes—mercy, humility, and devotion.

This passage offers a window into the personal character of one of Islam's great theologians. It is not a theological argument but a biographical sketch that reveals how his knowledge translated into ethical perfection. As you read, notice how each virtue flows from his deep awareness of God.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the virtues
Read the Arabic and translation once. List all the virtues mentioned, from 'khayr' to 'sabur'—there are at least eight specific character traits.
Pay attention to the sequence: goodness, righteousness, piety, abstinence, asceticism, forbearance, patience.
2
Reflect on knowledge and character
Notice that the passage begins by linking his ethics to his vast knowledge. Why do you think the biographer starts there? Knowledge in Islam is meant to produce character.
3
Consider the summary statement
The passage ends with 'his clay was luminous and his conduct surrounded by divine care'. What does this tell us about how his virtues were viewed? This shows that his virtues were seen as divinely gifted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبس من عظيم اخلاق الله تعالى للإمام السنوسي إلى عظيم علمه وبحبوحة معرفتِه . . سعة الأخلاق الحميدة ، فجابَ شُعب الإيمان وطنَّبَ فيها خيامه ، فعُهِدَ عنه أنه خيرٌ برٌّ ، تقي ورع زاهد ، حليم صبور ، سكنتِ الرحمة فؤاده ، وغلبت عليه الشفقة على جميع خلق الله تعالى ، هين لينُ القياد ، شديد الحياء ، كثير التواضع ، قليل الكلام والضحك تجلّى عليه الخوف من الله تعالى ؛ فأكثر من إحياء الليل مناجياً ، وأكثر من الصدقة والدعاء راجياً وبالجملة : كانت طينته نورانية ، وسيرته محفوفة بعناية ربانية .
A spark of the great ethics of God Almighty to Imam al-Sanusi, in addition to his vast knowledge and expanse of his understanding... the breadth of praiseworthy character, so he traversed the branches of faith and pitched his tents therein. It was known of him that he was good, righteous, pious, abstinent, ascetic, forbearing, patient. Mercy inhabited his heart, and compassion for all of God's creation overcame him. He was easygoing, gentle in leadership, extremely shy, very humble, little in speech and laughter. The fear of God became manifest upon him, so he frequently revived the night in intimate prayer, and frequently gave charity and supplication hoping. In summary: his clay was luminous, and his conduct was surrounded by divine care.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a description of Imam al-Sanusi's personal character and ethical qualities. It begins by stating that his ethical virtues are a spark from God's own attributes, alongside his vast knowledge. The author then enumerates his virtues: he is good (khayr), righteous (birr), pious (taqī), abstinent (wariʿ), ascetic (zāhid), forbearing (ḥalīm), patient (ṣabūr). His heart is filled with mercy (rahma) and he has overwhelming compassion (shafaqa) for all creation. He is easygoing and gentle (hayyin layyin al-qiyād), extremely shy (shadīd al-ḥayāʾ), very humble (kathīr al-tawāḍuʿ), and speaks and laughs little. The fear of God (khawf) is evident upon him, leading him to spend nights in intimate prayer (munājāt) and to give much charity and supplication (ṣadaqa wa duʿāʾ) hopefully. The summary concludes that his nature (ṭīnatuhu) was luminous (nūrāniyya) and his conduct (sīratuhu) was enveloped in divine care (ʿināya rabbāniyya).
