Key Terms
كرامات
توسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawassul is a form of shirk (polytheism) because it involves asking a created being for help.
Correction: The story shows that tawassul is seeking intercession through a righteous person's rank with Allah, not independent power. Sanusi himself taught it, showing its legitimacy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the meat not cook?
A) The meat was old and spoiled.
B) It was a sign that those who pray behind Sanusi are safe from hellfire.
C) The man had forgotten to say Bismillah.
D) The woman's key was lost because of sin.

Key Takeaway
Seeking intercession through righteous saints is a legitimate practice, and their connection to Allah can manifest in tangible divine assistance and protection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The meat miracle shows that praying behind a righteous imam can protect you from the fire of Hell. Does your choice of imam in prayer matter to you? Will you seek out a teacher or prayer leader whose connection to Allah elevates your own?
?
When you lose something precious, like the woman's key, do you panic or remember to use tawassul? How can you make it a habit to call upon Allah through the righteous before exhausting worldly efforts?
?
Sanusi told the man to 'keep that secret' – he did not seek fame for his miracle. When you receive a blessing or a sign from Allah, do you share it for attention or conceal it for humility? Examine your heart: are you seeking Allah or the admiration of people?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
4 min
Early Scholarly Feat: The Great Commentary
Sanusi's authorship of a major commentary at age 19 and the master's protective order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's early scholarly achievement of composing a major commentary at age nineteen, and the reaction of the spiritual master who ordered it hidden to protect him from the evil eye.

Core Idea
Sanusi's prodigious scholarship was recognized as peerless, yet required protection from envy.

Among Sanusi's listed miracles, his biographer includes his authorship of a commentary on al-Hawfiyya at just nineteen years of age. When the spiritual master al-Hasan Abarkan saw it, he praised it as having no equal and ordered it hidden until Sanusi turned forty to protect him from the evil eye. This lesson highlights how exceptional scholarly attainment can itself be a form of divine favor, while also requiring humility and caution against envy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note the details: the book's name (al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi), Sanusi's age, and the master's reaction.
The master says 'لا نظير له فيما أعلم' (there is no peer for it to my knowledge).
2
Understand the master's concern
Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan ordered the commentary hidden until Sanusi completed forty years. Why? To protect him from the evil eye (العين). This reflects a common belief that exceptional talent can attract envy and harm.
This shows the spiritual master's care for Sanusi's well-being.
3
Reflect on the significance
This 'miracle' is not a supernatural event but a remarkable intellectual feat at a young age. The biographer includes it as a karamah, indicating that exceptional knowledge and its recognition can be a sign of divine favor.

Source Text

They wanted to throw it away, but it was in its state with its blood. They said: Perhaps it is old meat. So they kept kindling fire on it until morning, but it did not change from its state! So the man remembered, and went to the Imam and informed him of that. He said: O my son; I hope from Allah the Exalted that everyone who prays behind me, the fire will not overcome him; perhaps this meat was with you when you prayed with me, but keep that secret. That: he used to say, trusting in his Lord: "Whoever has a need from Allah, let him seek intercession through us and put us forward." It is narrated that a woman lost the key to her house, and she tried every trick to open it but failed. So she sought intercession through the Shaykh and his standing with his Lord, and the door opened and the lock came undone. And among his miracles: his authorship of the great commentary on al-Hawfiyya, which he named al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi; he wrote it when he was nineteen years old. When Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan came across it, he marveled at it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye, and he said to him: There is no peer for it to my knowledge, and he made supplication for its author.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a hagiographical section recounting several miracles (karamat) attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Sanusi, as well as one of his early scholarly achievements. The author begins by stating that Imam al-Sanusi's stature does not depend on miracles, but that relating them serves to increase respect and honor. Then he notes that some of these miracles are mixed with the science of kalam, showing his sincerity in pursuing this science. The first story: A saint saw al-Sanusi's father in a dream after his death; the father said Allah forgave him because of his son's reflection on a mountain at the time of his burial. Al-Sanusi confirmed that he was indeed contemplating the mountain's composition by divine power and wisdom. The second story: A man entered the mosque carrying raw meat, prayed behind al-Sanusi, then the meat would not cook despite long boiling and burning; al-Sanusi interpreted this as a sign that those who pray behind him are safe from hellfire, and told the man to conceal the incident. The third: Al-Sanusi used to teach people to seek intercession (tawassul) through him. A woman who lost her key tried everything and then sought his intercession; the door opened miraculously. The fourth: At age nineteen, al-Sanusi authored a commentary on al-Hawfiyya called al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi. The spiritual master al-Hasan Abarkan, upon seeing it, ordered it hidden until the author reached forty to protect him from the evil eye, praising it as without peer.

Key Terms
كرامات
شيخ القطب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The commentary was hidden because it contained errors or unorthodox views.
Correction: It was hidden because it was exceptionally good, and the master feared the evil eye would harm the young author.

Checkpoint
Why did Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan order Sanusi's commentary to be hidden?
A) It contained doctrinal errors that needed correction.
B) He wanted to wait until Sanusi was older to avoid the evil eye.
C) The book was too long and needed editing.
D) He wanted to keep it as a secret legacy.

Key Takeaway
Exceptional scholarly attainment can be a form of divine favor, but humility demands protection from envy and the evil eye.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever recognized a unique gift or talent God has given you, and how do you protect it from the envy of others? Are you willing to follow wise counsel to conceal your blessings when necessary?
?
When you see exceptional success in others, do you feel genuine joy or a twinge of envy? How does this story challenge you to change your heart towards others' achievements?
?
What is one area of your life where you need to seek the protection and du'a of a righteous person, just as Sanusi received from his master? Will you take a step today to ask for spiritual covering?

The Miracle of Meat Preserved After Prayer Behind Imam Sanusi
Narrates a karamah of Imam Sanusi regarding meat preservation.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A saint's prayer can preserve even meat from decay.

This story from the life of Imam Sanusi illustrates a karamah—a miracle granted by Allah to His righteous servants. The incident shows how barakah (blessing) can affect physical objects. As you read the narrative, notice the Imam's humility and his instruction to the man to keep the matter secret. This reflects the Sunnah of saints who avoid fame.

Guided Path

This is not a natural occurrence; it is attributed to barakah from the prayer.
3
Reflect on Imam Sanusi's response
The Imam expresses hope that whoever prays behind him will be protected from fire, and he instructs the man to keep the matter secret. Consider why he did not want the miracle publicized.

Sanusi's Precocious Commentary and the Evil Eye
A biographical account of Sanusi's early commentary and its concealment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Imam Sanusi writing a major commentary at age nineteen and the reason for its concealment.

Core Idea
Youthful genius was hidden to protect from envy.

This lesson recounts a remarkable event in Imam Sanusi's early life. At just nineteen, he authored a major commentary that amazed a renowned saint. But instead of praise and acclaim, the saint ordered it hidden. Why? The answer reveals deep spiritual wisdom about jealousy and divine protection.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the details: the title of the commentary, the age of the author, and the reaction of al-Shaykh al-Hasan Abarkan.
The ellipsis in the Arabic indicates a pause in the narration.
2
Understand the concept of al-ayn
The saint ordered the commentary hidden 'lest he be struck by the evil eye.' Learn what the evil eye (al-ayn) means in Islamic tradition and why it was feared for someone so young and accomplished.
The evil eye is real and can harm, as affirmed in hadith.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider the wisdom of the saint's instruction. Sometimes blessings are concealed to protect them until the right time. Why might forty years have been the threshold?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك : تأليفه للشرح الكبير لـ « الحوفية » ، الذي سماه : المقرب المستوفي » ، ألفه وهو ابن تسع عشرة سنة ، فلما وقف عليه الشيخ القطب الحسن أبركان . . تعجب منه ، وأمر بإخفائه حتى يكمل مُؤلّفه أربعين سنة ؛ لئلا يصاب بالعين ، ويقول له : لا نظير له فيما أعلم ، ودعا لمؤلفه (۳)
And among that is: his authorship of the Great Commentary on al-Hawfiyyah, which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi'. He authored it when he was nineteen years old. When al-Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan came across it... he was amazed by it, and ordered it to be hidden until its author completed forty years, lest he be struck by the evil eye. And he said to him: 'There is nothing like it as far as I know,' and he prayed for its author.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage relates another remarkable event in Imam Sanusi's life: he authored a large commentary on a text called al-Hawfiyyah, which he named 'al-Muqrib al-Mustawfi' (The Inclusive Approximation), at the age of nineteen. When the eminent saint al-Shaykh al-Qutb al-Hasan Abarkan came across this work, he was amazed and ordered it to be hidden until the author reached the age of forty. The reason given was to protect him from the evil eye (al-ayn), as such extraordinary achievement at a young age could attract envy. The Shaykh also praised it saying there is nothing like it in his knowledge, and he prayed for the author. This demonstrates both the scholarly precocity of Imam Sanusi and the concern of the spiritual masters for protecting their pupils from jealousy.

The Scholar's Last Prayer and Angelic Command
Narrates the scholar's final illness and angelic visitation commanding him to abandon a practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances of the scholar's final illness and the spiritual vision that led him to abandon a devotional practice in obedience to a divine command.

Core Idea
Even in his final moments, the scholar's immediate response to divine instruction was total obedience.

This lesson presents a touching narrative from the end of the scholar's life. After leading his last prayer with great difficulty, he experiences an unconscious vision where angels take him to the heavens and he is commanded to leave something. His response demonstrates the height of his spiritual submission. As you read, consider what his actions reveal about his relationship with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the sequence of events. Note the key details: the last prayer, the food refusal, the unconsciousness, the vision.
Pay attention to the term 'المحبس'.
2
Reflect on the scholar's state
Consider why the scholar initially says 'I have lagged behind' and then becomes unconscious. What might that indicate about his spiritual awareness?
This shows his constant self-accountability.
3
Examine the vision and command
Identify what the angelic ascent entails and the command given. What is he told to leave?
He is commanded to leave 'what you are doing' and is told his term is near.
4
Understand his response
The scholar immediately abandons 'المحبس' and vows never to take anything from it. What does this tell us about his obedience?
He doesn't hesitate; he fully submits.
5
Consider the misunderstanding
The term 'المحبس' may be misinterpreted as a prison. In context, it likely refers to a devotional practice. How does this clarification affect understanding?
This prevents a wrong understanding of the scholar's action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصعود إلى المسجد ، وصلى بالناس صلاة عصر يوم الجمعة ، ولم يكمل الصلاة إلا بشق النفس ، وهذه آخر صلاة صلاها • فرجع إلى داره ، فبقي إلى صبيحة يوم السبت من الغد ، فقربت إليه زوجته طعاماً ، فقال لها : لا أقدر على شيء فقالت له : وأيُّ شيء بك ؟ فقال لها : أنا تخلفت ، ثم غاب عن حسّه ، فبقي على تلك الحالة النهار كله ثم • كلمته زوجته وقالت له : ما الذي غيّبك عن حِسَّكَ ؟ أو قريباً من هذا ، فقال لها : إنَّ الملائكة قد صعدت بي إلى السماء الدنيا ، فسمعت قائلاً يقول لي : اترك ما أنت عليه فقد قَرُبَ أَجلُكَ ، ثم قال : لا أستطيع أن أفسِّر لك بقية ما رأيت ، أو كما قال حبس فقالت له زوجته : وما الذي أُمرت بتركه ؟ قال لها : قد تركت ذلك المحبس لا آخذ منه شيئاً أبداً .
He climbed to the mosque and led the people in the afternoon prayer on Friday, and he did not complete the prayer except with difficulty of breath, and this was the last prayer he prayed. Then he returned to his home and remained until the morning of Saturday the next day. His wife offered him food, and he said to her: 'I cannot do anything.' She said to him: 'What is the matter with you?' He said to her: 'I have lagged behind.' Then he became unconscious and remained in that state all day. Then his wife spoke to him and said: 'What has taken away your senses?' or something close to this. He said to her: 'The angels ascended with me to the lowest heaven, and I heard a speaker saying to me: Leave what you are doing, for your term has drawn near. Then he said: I cannot explain to you the rest of what I saw, or as he said: [حبس]. His wife said to him: What have you been ordered to leave? He said to her: I have left that [المحبس] and will never take anything from it ever.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing the onset of the scholar's final illness. It begins with his struggle to complete the Friday afternoon prayer due to physical weakness, marking that as his last prayer. After returning home, he refuses food, saying 'I have lagged behind,' then falls unconscious. Upon regaining awareness, he tells his wife that angels took him to the lowest heaven, where a voice commanded him to abandon something he was doing because his death was near. He declines to explain further, but when his wife presses him about what he was ordered to leave, he states that he has given up that 'حبس' (a term that likely refers to a spiritual practice or physical object of devotion) and will never take anything from it again. This shows his immediate obedience to the divine command and his readiness for death.

Key Terms
المحبس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'المحبس' refers to a physical prison.
Correction: In context, 'المحبس' refers to a devotional practice or object the scholar was attached to; his command to leave it indicates he was too attached to a spiritual exercise that was no longer appropriate for him in his final state.

?

?
When the scholar said 'I have lagged behind', he felt he had fallen short despite a life of devotion. If you were told your death is near, what would you feel you have 'lagged behind' in? Write down one specific area and commit to a change today.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
The Scholar's Final Moments: Patience and Presence
Describes the scholar's final three days, suffering, steadfastness, and last words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scholar's final moments exemplify steadfast faith and spiritual awareness despite intense physical suffering.

Core Idea
True faith remains firm even when the body fails.

This passage recounts the last three days of the scholar's life, describing his illness, his patience, and his unwavering spiritual presence. As you read, notice how his physical weakness contrasts with his mental clarity and devotion to Allah. The narrative provides a powerful example of how a believer faces death with dignity and trust.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the English translation. Let the narrative flow and key events sink in before interpreting.
Pay attention to the details of his physical state and his responses.
2
Identify key moments of spiritual awareness
Look for instances where the scholar demonstrates mindfulness of Allah despite his pain: his response to the shahada prompting, his reassurance to his daughter, and his remark when the prayer beads fall.
3
Reflect on the significance of each interaction
Consider what each exchange reveals about his state of mind and faith. With his nephew, he shows he is not forgetful. With his daughter, he points to Paradise. With the beads, he notes that formal worship has ended.
These show his complete presence with Allah.
4
Consider the lesson for our own lives
Think about how this account teaches us about facing trials and death. The scholar's patience and spiritual focus even in agony is a model for believers.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه لازم الفراش من حينئذ إلى أن توفي ، ومدة مرضه عشرة أيام ، وفي كل ساعة يتقوَّى مرضه وتضاعف ألمه وتضعف قوته وحركته ، ويثقل لسانه ، وهو مع ذلك ثابت العقل [لم] يتأوه ولا أنَّ بالكلية ، ثم تجده مع ذلك يكلّم من كلمه ، ويسلم على من سلَّم عليه أو يشير له (۱) وقد ذكر الملالي في ( المواهب القدسية » ( ق ۱۳ ) أنه بلغ به الجهد حتى عجز عن التيمم وأركان الصلاة ، فقال : ( رحم الله تعالى أبا حنيفة حيث قال بسقوطها ) يعني : الصلاة . فلمَّا قَرُب أجلُهُ بثلاثة أيام دخلته سكرات الموت ، فرجع يتأوه بالقهر ويميل يميناً وشمالاً ، فنظرت إليه وقد احمرت وجنتاه وأرخيت عيناه وشفتاه (۱) ، واشتدَّ نَفَسُهُ ، وتقوَّى صعوده وهبوطه ، فلم أملك صبراً على البكاء بما عاينت من شدة مقاساته وعظيم صبره على ذلك ، وظننتُ أنه لا يبقى تلك الليلة ، وكانت ليلة السبت ، فبقي في تلك الليلة والأحد إلى بعد العصر ، فكان ابن أخيه حينئذ يلقنه الشهادة مرة بعد مرة ، فالتفت الشيخ له وقال بكلام ضعيف جداً : وهل ثَمَّ غيرها ؟ ! يعني : أنه رضي الله تعالى عنه ليس بغافل عنها بقلبه في هذا الوقت ، وإن كنت لم أنطق بها اللسان ففارقته النزع فحينئذ استبشروا بذلك ، وعرف الحاضرون أنه ثابت العقل ، ليس بغافل عن الله سبحانه وكانت بنته رضي الله عنها تقول له حينئذ : تمشي وتتركني ؟! فقال لها : الجنة تجمعنا عن قريب إن شاء الله تعالى مر ضه وكانت في يده رضي الله تعالى عنه سبحة ، فلما اشتدَّ سقطت السبحة من يده ، فبقي كذلك ما شاء الله ، ثم التفت إلى السبحة فلم يجدها في يده ، فقال : مشت العبادة يا محمد ؛ يعني : نفسه • وكان رضي الله عنه يقول عند موته : نسأله سبحانه أن يجعلنا (۱) وانظر هنا » المواهب القدسية » ( ق ٩٣ )
Then he kept to bed from then until he died, and his illness lasted ten days. Every hour his illness grew stronger, his pain doubled, his strength and movement weakened, and his tongue became heavy. Yet with all that, his mind was steadfast; he did not groan nor complain at all. Moreover, he would speak to whoever spoke to him and greet whoever greeted him or gesture to him. (1) Al-Malali mentioned in al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya (folio 13) that the effort reached him to the extent that he was unable to perform dry ablution and the pillars of prayer, and he said: 'May Allah have mercy on Abu Hanifa, for he ruled that prayer is waived' meaning prayer. When his death approached by three days, the throes of death entered him, and he began to groan with distress and sway right and left. I looked at him and his cheeks had reddened, his eyes had drooped, and his lips had relaxed (1), his breath intensified, and his rising and falling grew strong. I could not control myself from weeping due to what I witnessed of the severity of his suffering and the greatness of his patience upon it. I thought he would not survive that night, and it was Saturday night. He remained that night and Sunday until after afternoon. His nephew was then prompting him to recite the testimony of faith time after time. The shaykh turned to him and said with very weak speech: 'Is there anything else?!' meaning—may Allah be pleased with him—that he was not unmindful of it in his heart at that time, even if I did not utter it with the tongue. Then the agony left him. They rejoiced at that, and those present knew that his mind was steadfast and he was not unmindful of Allah, the Glorious. His daughter—may Allah be pleased with her—was saying to him then: 'You will go and leave me?!' He said to her: 'Paradise will gather us soon, Allah willing.' He had a prayer beads in his hand—may Allah be pleased with him—and when the pain intensified, the prayer beads fell from his hand. He remained as such for what Allah willed, then he turned to the prayer beads and did not find them in his hand, and he said: 'The worship has departed, O Muhammad' meaning himself. He—may Allah be pleased with him—was saying at his death: 'We ask Him, the Glorious, to make us...' (1) See here: al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya (folio 93).
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage continues the biography, describing the final phase of the scholar's illness. It opens by noting that after the events of the previous lesson, he took to bed for ten days, during which his condition progressively worsened: his pain increased, his strength and mobility decreased, and his speech became heavy. Despite this, he remained of sound mind and did not moan or complain. He continued to interact with those around him, speaking and returning greetings. A footnote cites al-Malalī's al-Mawāhib al-Qudusiyya, reporting that his suffering became so severe that he was unable to perform dry ablution (tayammum) or the essential acts of prayer, and he invoked mercy on Abū Ḥanīfa, who ruled that prayer is waived in such circumstances. Three days before his death, the throes of death (sakarāt al-mawt) began: he groaned, swayed, his cheeks reddened, eyes drooped, lips relaxed, and breathing grew labored. The narrator, overwhelmed by the severity of his suffering and his patience, wept. Though death seemed imminent on Saturday night, he survived until Sunday afternoon. His nephew repeatedly prompted him to recite the shahāda (testimony of faith). The shaykh turned to him and said weakly: 'Is there anything else?!' meaning that he was not forgetful of the shahāda in his heart, even if he did not pronounce it with his tongue. The onlookers understood from this that he was still fully conscious and mindful of Allah. His daughter asked him how he could leave her; he replied that Paradise would reunite them soon. During the height of his agony, the prayer beads (subḥa) he was holding fell from his hand. When he noticed their absence, he said: 'The worship has departed, O Muhammad'—referring to himself, as if the beads symbolized his devotion and now the time for formal worship had ended. Finally, he was heard praying: 'We ask Him, the Glorious, to make us...' (the sentence is incomplete in the text). This account emphasizes his unwavering spiritual presence and acceptance of divine decree throughout his final moments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scholar's groaning and physical distress indicate a lack of faith or impatience.
Correction: The narrator emphasizes that he was 'ثابت العقل' (steadfast in mind) and the scene with the shahāda shows his spiritual awareness was intact, not that his suffering contradicted his faith.

Checkpoint
What was the shaykh's response when his nephew repeatedly prompted him to recite the shahāda?
A) He recited it loudly.
B) He said 'Is there anything else?!' implying he was not unmindful of it in his heart.
C) He remained silent.
D) He asked for water.

Key Takeaway
The scholar's final moments show that true devotion to Allah remains steady even in the most extreme physical distress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your body fails and pain overwhelms you, what will your heart be occupied with? Are you training your soul now to find Allah even when words and actions are impossible?
?
The shaykh answered his daughter's plea with certainty about Paradise. Do you long for the next world enough to release your grip on this one? What would it take for you to say 'Paradise will gather us soon' with the same conviction?
?
You will leave this world as you find it. The beads fell, the tongue stopped—but the heart remained. What outward acts of worship do you cling to that might become a veil between you and Allah in your final moments? How can you ensure your heart stays connected beyond rituals?
